      <p><b>Ghana</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Ghana.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/En-us-Ghana.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Ghana.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Ghana</b>, is a country along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Subregion" title="Subregion">subregion</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. Spanning a <a href="/wiki/Landmass" title="Landmass">land mass</a> of 238,535&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (92,099&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Ghana is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ghana%E2%80%93Ivory_Coast_border" title="Ghana–Ivory Coast border">the west</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso%E2%80%93Ghana_border" title="Burkina Faso–Ghana border">the north</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ghana%E2%80%93Togo_border" title="Ghana–Togo border">the east</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the Atlantic Ocean in the south. <i>Ghana</i> means "Warrior King" in the <a href="/wiki/Soninke_language" title="Soninke language">Soninke language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-warriorking_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warriorking-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first permanent state in the territory of present-day Ghana dates back to the 11th century, the <a href="/wiki/Bono_state" title="Bono state">Bono State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Numerous kingdoms and empires emerged over the centuries, of which the most powerful were the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dagbon" title="Kingdom of Dagbon">Kingdom of Dagbon</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Beginning in the 15th century, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>, followed by numerous other European powers, contested the area for trading rights, until the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> ultimately established control of the coast by the late 19th century. Following over a century of native resistance, what are now Ghana's borders follow the lines of what were four separate British colonial territories: <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(Crown_Colony)" title="Ashanti (Crown Colony)">Ashanti</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territories_of_the_Gold_Coast_(British_protectorate)" title="Northern Territories of the Gold Coast (British protectorate)">Northern Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Togoland" title="British Togoland">British Togoland</a>. These were unified as an independent <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominion</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> on 6 March 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-Universal_Newsreel_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Universal_Newsreel-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_For_Sub-Saharan_Africa_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_For_Sub-Saharan_Africa-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Exploring_Africa_–_Decolinization_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exploring_Africa_–_Decolinization-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's population of approximately 30&nbsp;million<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> spans a variety of ethnic, linguistic and religious groups.<sup id="cite_ref-popest_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popest-5">[5]</a></sup> According to the 2010 census, 71.2% of the population was Christian, 17.6% was <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a>, and 5.2% practised traditional faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2010_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2010-18">[18]</a></sup> Its diverse geography and ecology ranges from coastal savannahs to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rain forests</a>. </p>
      <p>Ghana is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">constitutional democracy</a> led by a president who is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of the government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_CIA_World_FactBook_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_CIA_World_FactBook-19">[19]</a></sup> Ghana's growing economic prosperity and democratic political system have made it a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-South_America_and_West_Africa_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_America_and_West_Africa-20">[20]</a></sup> It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS), <a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">Group of 24</a> (G24) and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymology</a> of the name <i>Ghana</i> means "<a href="/wiki/Warriors" class="mw-redirect" title="Warriors">Strong Warrior</a> King" and was the title accorded to the kings of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, but the empire was further north than the modern nation of Ghana, in <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">the region of Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etymology_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etymology-22">[22]</a></sup> Ghana was known for its large Gold usage, and hence was named the <i>Land of Gold</i><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">Trans-Saharan trade</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Akan_face.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Akan_face.jpg/170px-Akan_face.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Akan_face.jpg/255px-Akan_face.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Akan_face.jpg/340px-Akan_face.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Akan_face.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>16th-century <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> Terracotta, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg/220px-Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg/330px-Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg/440px-Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1008" data-file-height="717"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_from_Milner%27s_Atlas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An 1850 map showing the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ashanti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Ashanti">Kingdom of Ashanti</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">Guinea region</a> and surrounding regions in West Africa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lidded_Vessel_(Kuduo)_MET_DP108293.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg/220px-Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg/330px-Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg/440px-Lidded_Vessel_%28Kuduo%29_MET_DP108293.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="1960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lidded_Vessel_(Kuduo)_MET_DP108293.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>18th-century Ashanti brass <i>kuduo</i>. Gold dust and nuggets were kept in <i>kuduo</i>, as were other items of personal value and significance. As receptacles for their owners' <i>kra</i>, or life force, <i>kuduo</i> were prominent features of ceremonies designed to honour and protect that individual.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ghana" title="History of Ghana">History of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_kingdoms">Medieval kingdoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Medieval kingdoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dagbon" title="Kingdom of Dagbon">Kingdom of Dagbon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana was recognised as one of the great kingdoms in <a href="/wiki/Bilad_el-Sudan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilad el-Sudan">Bilad el-Sudan</a> by the ninth century.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana was inhabited in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> by a number of ancient predominantly <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> kingdoms in the Southern and Central territories. This included the <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bonoman" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonoman">Bonoman</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denkyira" title="Denkyira">Denkyira</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mankessim_Kingdom" title="Mankessim Kingdom">Mankessim Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the area of present-day Ghana in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> has experienced many population movements, the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akans</a> were firmly settled by the 5th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> By the early 11th century, the Akans were firmly established in the Akan state called <a href="/wiki/Bonoman" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonoman">Bonoman</a>, for which the <a href="/wiki/Brong-Ahafo_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brong-Ahafo Region">Brong-Ahafo Region</a> is named.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From the 13th century, Akans emerged from what is believed to have been the Bonoman area, to create several Akan states of Ghana, mainly based on gold trading.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> These states included Bonoman (<a href="/wiki/Brong-Ahafo_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brong-Ahafo Region">Brong-Ahafo Region</a>), Ashanti (<a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Region" title="Ashanti Region">Ashanti Region</a>), <a href="/wiki/Denkyira" title="Denkyira">Denkyira</a> (<a href="/wiki/Central_Region,_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Region, Ghana">Western North region</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mankessim_Kingdom" title="Mankessim Kingdom">Mankessim Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Western_Region,_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Region, Ghana">Central region</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Region,_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Region, Ghana">(Eastern region)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup> By the 19th century, the territory of the southern part of Ghana was included in the <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Kingdom of Ashanti</a>, one of the most influential states in sub-saharan Africa prior to the onset of colonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government of the Ashanti Empire operated first as a loose network, and eventually as a centralised kingdom with an advanced, highly specialised bureaucracy centred in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Kumasi" title="Kumasi">Kumasi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup> Prior to Akan contact with Europeans, the Akan people created an advanced economy based on principally gold and <a href="/wiki/Gold_bar" title="Gold bar">gold bar</a> <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">commodities</a> then traded with the states of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The earliest known kingdoms to emerge in modern Ghana were the <a href="/wiki/Oti%E2%80%93Volta_languages" title="Oti–Volta languages">Mole-Dagbani</a> states.<sup id="cite_ref-col_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-26">[26]</a></sup> The Mole-Dagomba came on horseback from present-day <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> under a single leader, <a href="/wiki/Na_Gbewa" title="Na Gbewa">Naa Gbewaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> With their advanced weapons and based on a central authority, they easily invaded and occupied the lands of the local people ruled by the <i>Tendamba</i> (land god priests), established themselves as the rulers over the locals, and made <a href="/wiki/Gambaga" title="Gambaga">Gambaga</a> their capital.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The death of Naa Gbewaa caused civil war among his children, some of whom broke off and founded separate states including <a href="/wiki/Dagomba_people" title="Dagomba people">Dagbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamprusi_people" title="Mamprusi people">Mamprugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Kingdoms" title="Mossi Kingdoms">Mossi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanumba_people" title="Nanumba people">Nanumba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wala_people" title="Wala people">Wala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="European_contact_.2815th_century.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact_(15th_century)">European contact (15th century)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European contact (15th century)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast (region)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Gold_Coast" title="Portuguese Gold Coast">Portuguese Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Gold_Coast" title="Dutch Gold Coast">Dutch Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Slave_Coast" title="Dutch Slave Coast">Dutch Slave Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Gold_Coast" title="Swedish Gold Coast">Swedish Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_Gold_Coast" title="Danish Gold Coast">Danish Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandenburger_Gold_Coast" title="Brandenburger Gold Coast">Brandenburger Gold Coast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast (British colony)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Elmina_slave_castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Elmina_slave_castle.jpg/220px-Elmina_slave_castle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Elmina_slave_castle.jpg/330px-Elmina_slave_castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Elmina_slave_castle.jpg/440px-Elmina_slave_castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="872"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Elmina_slave_castle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Gold_Coast" title="Portuguese Gold Coast">Portuguese Gold Coast</a> with the construction of <a href="/wiki/Elmina_Castle" title="Elmina Castle">Elmina Castle</a> (<i>Castelo da Mina</i>) by <a href="/wiki/Diogo_de_Azambuja" title="Diogo de Azambuja">Diogo de Azambuja</a> in 1482, making it the oldest <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonial_architecture" title="Portuguese colonial architecture">European building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Akan trade with European states began after contact with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> in the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Early European contact by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese people</a>, who came to the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast region</a> in the 15th century to trade and then established the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Gold_Coast" title="Portuguese Gold Coast">Portuguese Gold Coast</a> (Costa do Ouro), focused on the extensive availability of gold.<sup id="cite_ref-History_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-36">[36]</a></sup> The Portuguese built a trading lodge at a coastal settlement called Anomansah (the perpetual drink) which they renamed <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">São Jorge da Mina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1481, King <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">John II of Portugal</a> commissioned <a href="/wiki/Diogo_d%27Azambuja" class="mw-redirect" title="Diogo d'Azambuja">Don Diego d'Azambuja</a> to build the <a href="/wiki/Elmina_Castle" title="Elmina Castle">Elmina Castle</a>, which was completed in three years.<sup id="cite_ref-History_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-36">[36]</a></sup> By 1598, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> had joined the Portuguese in the gold trade, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Gold_Coast" title="Dutch Gold Coast">Dutch Gold Coast</a> (Nederlandse Bezittingen ter Kuste van Guinea) and building forts at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Komenda" title="Fort Komenda">Fort Komenda</a> and Kormantsi.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_book_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_book-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1617, the Dutch captured the Olnini Castle from the Portuguese, and <a href="/wiki/Axim" title="Axim">Axim</a> in 1642 (<a href="/wiki/Fort_Saint_Anthony" title="Fort Saint Anthony">Fort St Anthony</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_book_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_book-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other European traders had joined in gold trading by the mid-17th century, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedes</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Gold_Coast" title="Swedish Gold Coast">Swedish Gold Coast</a> (Svenska Guldkusten), and <a href="/wiki/Denmark-Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Denmark-Norway">Denmark-Norway</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Gold_Coast" title="Danish Gold Coast">Danish Gold Coast</a> (Danske Guldkyst <i>or</i> Dansk Guinea).<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> merchants, impressed with the gold resources in the area, named it <i>Costa do Ouro</i> or <i>Gold Coast</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> Also beginning in the 17th century — in addition to the gold trade — Portuguese, Dutch, English, and French traders also participated in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-Emmer_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Emmer-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png/300px-British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png/450px-British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png/600px-British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png 2x" data-file-width="1694" data-file-height="1168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:British_Ransack_Fomena_Palace.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>During <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Ashanti_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Ashanti Wars">Anglo-Ashanti Wars</a> British troops ransacking a <a href="/wiki/Fomena" title="Fomena">Fomena</a> chief's palace en route to Kumasi in 1874
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>More than thirty forts and castles were built by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, Swedish, <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Dano-Norwegians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and German merchants; the latter <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> establishing the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburger_Gold_Coast" title="Brandenburger Gold Coast">German Gold Coast</a> (Brandenburger Gold Coast <i>or</i> Groß Friedrichsburg).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1874 Great Britain established control over some parts of the country, assigning these areas the status of <a href="/wiki/British_Gold_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="British Gold Coast">British Gold Coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-colestablish_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colestablish-41">[41]</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Engagement_(military)" title="Engagement (military)">military engagements</a> occurred between the British colonial powers and the various Akan nation-states. The Akan <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ashanti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Ashanti">Kingdom of Ashanti</a> defeated the British a few times in the 100-year-long <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Ashanti_wars" title="Anglo-Ashanti wars">Anglo-Ashanti wars</a> but eventually lost with the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Golden_Stool" title="War of the Golden Stool">War of the Golden Stool</a> in the early 1900s.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chronology_of_world_history_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronology_of_world_history-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_to_independence">Transition to independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Transition to independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kwame_Nkrumah_(JFKWHP-AR6409-A).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kwame Nkrumah" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-A%29.jpg/220px-Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-A%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-A%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kwame_Nkrumah_(JFKWHP-AR6409-A).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a>, first President of Ghana
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ghana" title="Dominion of Ghana">Dominion of Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Independence_Act_1957" title="Ghana Independence Act 1957">Ghana Independence Act 1957</a>
      </div>

           </div>

          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Celebrations marking Ghana's independence on 6 March 1957
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1947, the newly formed <a href="/wiki/United_Gold_Coast_Convention" title="United Gold Coast Convention">United Gold Coast Convention</a> (UGCC) led by <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Six_(Ghana)" title="The Big Six (Ghana)">"The Big Six"</a> called for "self-government within the shortest possible time" following the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_legislative_election,_1946" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Coast legislative election, 1946">Gold Coast legislative election, 1946</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a>, a Ghanaian nationalist who led Ghana from 1957 to 1966 as the country's first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ghana" title="Prime Minister of Ghana">Prime Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ghana" title="President of Ghana">President</a>, formed the <a href="/wiki/Convention_People%27s_Party" title="Convention People's Party">Convention People's Party</a> (CPP) in 1949 with the motto "self-government now".<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> The party initiated a "positive action" campaign involving non-violent protests, strikes and non-cooperation with the British authorities. Nkrumah was arrested and sentenced to one year imprisonment during this time. In the Gold Coast's <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_legislative_election,_1951" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Coast legislative election, 1951">February 1951 general election</a>, he was elected to Parliament and released from prison to become leader of government business.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> He became Prime Minister of the Gold Coast in 1952. He improved the infrastructure of the country and his Africanisation policies created better career opportunities for Ghanaians. </p>
      <p>On 6 March 1957 at 12&nbsp;midnight, the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(Crown_Colony)" title="Ashanti (Crown Colony)">Ashanti</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territories_of_the_Gold_Coast_(British_protectorate)" title="Northern Territories of the Gold Coast (British protectorate)">Northern Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Togoland" title="British Togoland">British Togoland</a> were unified as one single independent dominion within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a> under the name Ghana. This was done under the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Independence_Act_1957" title="Ghana Independence Act 1957">Ghana Independence Act 1957</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Ghana" title="Flag of Ghana">flag of Ghana</a>, consisting of the colours red, gold, green, and a black star, dates back to this unification.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_flag_and_description_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_flag_and_description-46">[46]</a></sup> It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Theodosia_Salome_Okoh" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodosia Salome Okoh">Theodosia Salome Okoh</a>; the red represents the blood that was shed towards independence, the gold represents the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial minerals</a> wealth of Ghana, the green symbolises the rich <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> of Ghana, and the black star is the symbol of the Ghanaian people and African emancipation.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 July 1960, following the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_constitutional_referendum,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian constitutional referendum, 1960">Ghanaian constitutional referendum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 1960">Ghanaian presidential election</a>, Nkrumah declared Ghana as a republic and assumed the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-Universal_Newsreel_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Universal_Newsreel-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_For_Sub-Saharan_Africa_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_For_Sub-Saharan_Africa-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Exploring_Africa_–_Decolinization_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exploring_Africa_–_Decolinization-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> 6 March is the nation's <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Ghana)" title="Independence Day (Ghana)">Independence Day</a> and 1 July is now celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day" title="Republic Day">Republic Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the time of independence Nkrumah declared, "My first objective is to abolish from Ghana poverty, ignorance, and disease. We shall measure our progress by the improvement in the health of our people; by the number of children in school, and by the quality of their education; by the availability of water and electricity in our towns and villages; and by the happiness which our people take in being able to manage their own affairs. The welfare of our people is our chief pride, and it is by this that the government will ask to be judged.".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nkrumah was the first African head of state to promote the concept of <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanism</a>, which he had been introduced to during his studies at <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_University_(Pennsylvania)" title="Lincoln University (Pennsylvania)">Lincoln University</a>, Pennsylvania in the United States, at the time when <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Garvey" title="Marcus Garvey">Marcus Garvey</a> was becoming famous for his "Back to Africa Movement".<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> Nkrumah merged the teachings of Garvey, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a> and the naturalised <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois" title="W. E. B. Du Bois">W. E. B. Du Bois</a> into the formation of 1960s Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Ghana_38-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Ghana-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Osagyefo Dr. Kwame Nkrumah, as he became known, played an instrumental part in the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, and in establishing the <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah_Ideological_Institute" title="Kwame Nkrumah Ideological Institute">Kwame Nkrumah Ideological Institute</a> to teach his ideologies of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> His life achievements were recognised by Ghanaians during his centenary birthday celebration, and the day was instituted as a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Ghana" title="Public holidays in Ghana">public holiday in Ghana</a> (<a href="/wiki/Founder%27s_Day_(Ghana)" class="mw-redirect" title="Founder's Day (Ghana)">Founder's Day</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_Cold_Chop_and_aftermath">Operation Cold Chop and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Operation Cold Chop and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ghana_(1966%E2%80%9379)" title="History of Ghana (1966–79)">History of Ghana (1966–79)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The government of Nkrumah was subsequently overthrown by a coup by the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Armed_Forces" title="Ghana Armed Forces">Ghana Armed Forces</a> codenamed "Operation Cold Chop". This occurred while Nkrumah was abroad with <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a> in the People's Republic of China, on a fruitless mission to <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> in Vietnam to help end the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. The coup took place on 24 February 1966, led by Col. <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Kwasi_Kotoka" title="Emmanuel Kwasi Kotoka">Emmanuel Kwasi Kotoka</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Council" title="National Liberation Council">National Liberation Council</a> (NLC) was formed, chaired by Lt. General <a href="/wiki/Joseph_A._Ankrah" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph A. Ankrah">Joseph A. Ankrah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-political_&amp;_social_thought_of_Kwame_Nkrumah_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-political_&amp;_social_thought_of_Kwame_Nkrumah-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A series of alternating military and civilian governments, often affected by economic instabilities,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> ruled Ghana from 1966 to 1981, ending with the ascension to power of <a href="/wiki/Flight_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight Lieutenant">Flight Lieutenant</a> <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" title="Jerry Rawlings">Jerry John Rawlings</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_National_Defence_Council" title="Provisional National Defence Council">Provisional National Defence Council</a> (PNDC) in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight_Lieutenant_Jerry_John_Rawlings_(J.J_Rawlings)_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight_Lieutenant_Jerry_John_Rawlings_(J.J_Rawlings)-55">[55]</a></sup> These changes resulted in the suspension of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ghana" title="Constitution of Ghana">Constitution of Ghana</a> in 1981, and the banning of <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties in Ghana">political parties in Ghana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rawlings:_The_legacy_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rawlings:_The_legacy-56">[56]</a></sup> The economy soon declined, so Rawlings negotiated a structural adjustment plan changing many old economic policies, and economic growth soon recovered during the mid-1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Rawlings:_The_legacy_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rawlings:_The_legacy-56">[56]</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ghana" title="Constitution of Ghana">Constitution of Ghana</a> restoring <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> politics was promulgated in <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 1992">Ghanaian presidential election, 1992</a>; Rawlings was elected as president of Ghana then, and again in <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_general_election,_1996" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian general election, 1996">Ghanaian general election, 1996</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Elections_in_Ghana_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elections_in_Ghana-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kpetoee.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kpetoee.jpg/220px-Kpetoee.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kpetoee.jpg/330px-Kpetoee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kpetoee.jpg/440px-Kpetoee.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kpetoee.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Chieftaincy" class="mw-redirect" title="Chieftaincy">chiefs</a> in Ghana in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Winning the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_general_election,_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian general election, 2000">2000 Ghanaian elections</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Kufuor" title="John Kufuor">John Agyekum Kufuor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_Patriotic_Party" title="New Patriotic Party">New Patriotic Party</a> (NPP) was sworn into office as president of Ghana on 7 January 2001, and attained the presidency again in the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_general_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian general election, 2004">2004 Ghanaian elections</a>, thus also serving two <a href="/wiki/Term_of_office" title="Term of office">terms</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Term_limit" title="Term limit">term limit</a>) as president of Ghana and thus marking the first time under the fourth republic that power was transferred from one legitimately elected <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> to another.<sup id="cite_ref-Elections_in_Ghana_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elections_in_Ghana-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nana Akufo-Addo, the ruling party candidate, was defeated in a very close election by <a href="/wiki/John_Atta_Mills" title="John Atta Mills">John Atta Mills</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Ghana)" title="National Democratic Congress (Ghana)">National Democratic Congress</a> (NDC) following the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 2008">Ghanaian presidential election, 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Mills died of natural causes and was succeeded by vice-president <a href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dramani Mahama">John Dramani Mahama</a> on 24 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 2012">Ghanaian presidential election, 2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Mahama" title="John Mahama">John Dramani Mahama</a> became President-elect and was inaugurated on 7 January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_President_John_Dramani_Mahama_sworn_in_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_President_John_Dramani_Mahama_sworn_in-61">[61]</a></sup> Ghana was a stable democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Elections_in_Ghana_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elections_in_Ghana-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 2016">Ghanaian presidential election, 2016</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nana_Akufo-Addo" title="Nana Akufo-Addo">Nana Akufo-Addo</a> became President-elect and was inaugurated as the fifth President of the Fourth Republic of Ghana and eighth President of Ghana on 7 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_timeline">Historical timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Historical timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div style="width:90%; overflow:scroll"> 
       <div class="timeline-wrapper">
        <map name="timeline_339782f2a7659cd11c90cb510fbd3192"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Nana_Akufo%2DAddo" coords="660,262,798,286" title="Nana Akufo-Addo" alt="Nana Akufo-Addo"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" coords="606,243,771,267" title="John Dramani Mahama" alt="John Dramani Mahama"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/John_Atta_Mills" coords="570,224,815,248" title="John Atta Mills" alt="John Atta Mills"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/John_Kufuor" coords="532,206,697,230" title="John Kufuor" alt="John Kufuor"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" coords="447,187,612,211" title="Jerry Rawlings" alt="Jerry Rawlings"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" coords="351,168,516,192" title="Jerry Rawlings" alt="Jerry Rawlings"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Hilla_Limann" coords="244,150,362,174" title="Hilla Limann" alt="Hilla Limann"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" coords="220,131,505,155" title="Jerry Rawlings" alt="Jerry Rawlings"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Fred_Akuffo" coords="216,112,615,136" title="Fred Akuffo" alt="Fred Akuffo"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Ignatius_Acheampong" coords="207,94,465,118" title="Ignatius Acheampong" alt="Ignatius Acheampong"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Edward_Akufo%2DAddo" coords="138,75,289,99" title="Edward Akufo-Addo" alt="Edward Akufo-Addo"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Nii_Amaa_Ollennu" coords="123,56,268,80" title="Nii Amaa Ollennu" alt="Nii Amaa Ollennu"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Akwasi_Afrifa" coords="122,38,367,62" title="Akwasi Afrifa" alt="Akwasi Afrifa"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Arthur_Ankrah" coords="108,19,320,43" title="Joseph Arthur Ankrah" alt="Joseph Arthur Ankrah"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" coords="75,0,260,24" title="Kwame Nkrumah" alt="Kwame Nkrumah"></map>
