      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ghana" title="Geography of Ghana">Geography of Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Ghana" title="Geology of Ghana">Geology of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;max-width:322px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:176px;max-width:176px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:203px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ghana_Topography.png/174px-Ghana_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="174" height="204" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ghana_Topography.png/261px-Ghana_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ghana_Topography.png/348px-Ghana_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="794" data-file-height="931"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Ghana-Togo <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a>−<a href="/wiki/Topographic_map" title="Topographic map">topographic map</a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:203px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_sat.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Ghana_sat.png/140px-Ghana_sat.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="203" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Ghana_sat.png/210px-Ghana_sat.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Ghana_sat.png/280px-Ghana_sat.png 2x" data-file-width="534" data-file-height="774"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Ghana <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">satellite image</a> from <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">outer space</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana is located on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a>, only a few degrees north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>, therefore giving it a warm climate.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Physical_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Physical-64">[64]</a></sup> Ghana spans an area of 238,535&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (92,099&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and has an Atlantic coastline that stretches 560 kilometres (350 miles) on the Gulf of Guinea in Atlantic Ocean to its south.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Physical_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Physical-64">[64]</a></sup> It lies between latitudes 4°45'N and 11°N, and longitudes 1°15'E and 3°15'W. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Meridian" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Meridian">Prime Meridian</a> passes through Ghana, specifically through the industrial <a href="/wiki/Port_town" class="mw-redirect" title="Port town">port town</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tema" title="Tema">Tema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Physical_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Physical-64">[64]</a></sup> Ghana is geographically closer to the "centre" of the Earth geographical coordinates than any other country; even though the notional centre, (0°, 0°) is located in the Atlantic Ocean approximately 614&nbsp;km (382&nbsp;mi) off the south-east coast of Ghana on the Gulf of Guinea. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">Grasslands</a> mixed with south coastal <a href="/wiki/Shrubland" title="Shrubland">shrublands</a> and forests dominate Ghana, with forest extending northward from the south-west coast of Ghana on the Gulf of Guinea in the Atlantic Ocean 320 kilometres (200 miles) and eastward for a maximum of about 270 kilometres (170 miles) with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ashanti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Ashanti">Kingdom of Ashanti</a> or the southern part of Ghana being a primary location for mining of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial minerals</a> and timber.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Physical_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Physical-64">[64]</a></sup> Ghana is home to five terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Guinean_forests" title="Eastern Guinean forests">Eastern Guinean forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_mangroves" title="Central African mangroves">Central African mangroves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-65">[65]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.53/10, ranking it 112<sup>nd</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> Ghana encompasses <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterfall" title="Waterfall">waterfalls</a>, low hills, rivers, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Volta" title="Lake Volta">Lake Volta</a>, the world's largest artificial lake, <a href="/wiki/Dodi_Island" title="Dodi Island">Dodi Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobowasi_Island" title="Bobowasi Island">Bobowasi Island</a> on the south Atlantic Ocean coast of Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_low_plains_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_low_plains-67">[67]</a></sup> The northernmost part of Ghana is Pulmakong and the southernmost part of Ghana is <a href="/wiki/Cape_Three_Points" title="Cape Three Points">Cape Three Points</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Physical_64-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Physical-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ghana" title="Climate of Ghana">Climate of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> of Ghana is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, and there are two main seasons: the <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_Climate_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP_Climate-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p>Ghana <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ghana" title="Climate of Ghana">sits at the intersection of three hydro-climatic zones</a>. Because of this, climate change is expected to impact Ghana in several ways.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:1-69">[69]</a></sup> Changes in <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> conditions and sea-level rise will affect the salinity of coastal waters. This is expected to negatively affect both farming and <a href="/wiki/Fisheries" class="mw-redirect" title="Fisheries">fisheries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:0_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:0-70">[70]</a></sup> The national economy stands to suffer from the impacts of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> because of its dependence on climate sensitive-sectors such as <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>. Moreover, access to freshwater is expected to become more challenging and reduced water supply will have a negative impact on hydropower which provides 54% of the country's electricity capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:0_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:0-70">[70]</a></sup> Additionally, Ghana will likely see more cases of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> since both are impacted by changes in water conditions. </p> In 2015, the government produced a document titled "Ghana's Intended Nationally Determined Contribution."<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Ghana_:2-71">[71]</a></sup> Following that, Ghana signed the Paris Climate Agreement in 2016.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">Government of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ghana" title="Politics of Ghana">Politics of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG/220px-Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG/330px-Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG/440px-Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="833" data-file-height="463"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Parliament_House_%E2%80%93_Ghana_Supreme_Court_%E2%80%93_Osu_Castle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_House_of_Ghana" title="Parliament House of Ghana">Parliament House of Ghana</a>, the Supreme Court of Ghana and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Ghana" title="Judiciary of Ghana">Judiciary of Ghana</a> buildings and <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_House" title="Jubilee House">Jubilee House</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_palace" title="Presidential palace">presidential palace</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG/220px-Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG/330px-Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG/440px-Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="452"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Presidents_of_Ghana_and_of_the_4th_Republic_of_Ghana.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>First President of the Republic of Ghana <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Nkrumah</a> and the 1st, 2nd, 3rd and 4th presidents of the 4th Republic of Ghana <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" title="Jerry Rawlings">Rawlings</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Kufuor" title="John Kufuor">Kufuor</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_Atta_Mills" class="mw-redirect" title="John Evans Atta Mills">Mills</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dramani Mahama">Mahama</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_executive_theory" title="Unitary executive theory">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional democracy">constitutional democracy</a> with a parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> that is dominated by two parties — the National Democratic Congress (NDC) and the New Patriotic Party (NPP). Ghana alternated between civilian and military governments until January 1993, when the military government gave way to the Fourth Republic of Ghana after <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_presidential_election,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian presidential election, 1992">presidential</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_parliamentary_election,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian parliamentary election, 1992">parliamentary elections</a> in late 1992. The 1992 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ghana" title="Constitution of Ghana">constitution of Ghana</a> divides powers among a <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander-in-Chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Armed_Forces" title="Ghana Armed Forces">Ghana Armed Forces</a> (<a href="/wiki/President_of_Ghana" title="President of Ghana">President of Ghana</a>), parliament (<a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Ghana" title="Parliament of Ghana">Parliament of Ghana</a>), cabinet (<a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ghana" title="Cabinet of Ghana">Cabinet of Ghana</a>), council of state (<a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Ghana)" title="Council of State (Ghana)">Ghanaian Council of State</a>), and an independent judiciary (<a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Ghana" title="Judiciary of Ghana">Judiciary of Ghana</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">Government of Ghana</a> is elected by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> after every four years.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nana_Akufo-Addo" title="Nana Akufo-Addo">Nana Akufo-Addo</a> won the Presidency in the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_general_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghanaian general election, 2016">Ghanaian general election</a> held on 7 December 2016, defeating incumbent <a href="/wiki/John_Mahama" title="John Mahama">John Mahama</a>. He was sworn in on 7 January 2017.He also won the 2020 election and was subsequently sworn in on 7th January 2021. Presidents can serve only two terms in office with each term having four years. The president can serve a second term only when he or she is re-elected .Ghana has never had a female president. </p>
      <p>The 2012 <a href="/wiki/Fragile_States_Index" title="Fragile States Index">Fragile States Index</a> indicated that Ghana is ranked the 67th least fragile state in the world and the 5th least fragile state in Africa after <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, 2nd <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, 3rd <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, and 4th South Africa. Ghana ranked 112th out of 177 countries on the index.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Ghana ranked as the 64th least <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corrupt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">politically corrupt</a> country in the world out of all 174 countries ranked and Ghana ranked as the 5th least corrupt and politically corrupt country in Africa out of 53 countries in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Transparency International Corruption Perception Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Ghana was ranked 7th in Africa out of 53 countries in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. The Ibrahim Index is a comprehensive measure of African government, based on a number of different variables which reflect the success with which governments deliver essential political goods to its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Ghana" title="Foreign relations of Ghana">Foreign relations of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg/220px-Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg/330px-Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg/440px-Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kofi_Annan_at_OYW.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, Ghanaian diplomat and United Nations Secretary-General 1997–2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since independence, Ghana has been devoted to ideals of nonalignment and is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Ghana favours international and regional political and economic co-operation, and is an active member of the United Nations and the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-H._E._Mr._Ken_Kanda_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H._E._Mr._Ken_Kanda-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana has a strong relationship with the United States. Three recent US presidents--<a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>—made diplomatic trips to Ghana. Many Ghanaian diplomats and politicians hold positions in international organisations, including Ghanaian diplomat and former <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, International Criminal Court Judge <a href="/wiki/Akua_Kuenyehia" title="Akua Kuenyehia">Akua Kuenyehia</a>, and former President <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings" title="Jerry Rawlings">Jerry John Rawlings</a> and former President <a href="/wiki/John_Kufuor" title="John Kufuor">John Agyekum Kufuor</a>, who both served as diplomats of the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2010, Ghana's former President <a href="/wiki/John_Atta_Mills" title="John Atta Mills">John Atta Mills</a> visited China on an official visit. Mills and China's former President <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a>, marked the 50th anniversary of diplomatic ties between the two nations, at the <a href="/wiki/Great_Hall_of_the_People" title="Great Hall of the People">Great Hall of the People</a> on 20 September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Hu_Jintao-John_Atta_Mills_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hu_Jintao-John_Atta_Mills-78">[78]</a></sup> China reciprocated with an official visit in November 2011, by the Vice-Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Standing_Committee_of_the_National_People%27s_Congress_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing Committee of the National People's Congress of China">Standing Committee of the National People's Congress of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Tienong" title="Zhou Tienong">Zhou Tienong</a> who visited Ghana and met with Ghana's President <a href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dramani Mahama">John Dramani Mahama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua2011_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua2011-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Islamic Republic of Iran</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Iran">6th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iran" title="President of Iran">President of Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a> met with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Ghana" title="List of heads of state of Ghana">12th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ghana" title="President of Ghana">President of Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dramani Mahama">John Dramani Mahama</a> on 16 April 2013 to hold discussions with President John Dramani Mahama on strengthening the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and also co–chair a bilateral meeting between Ghana and Iran at the Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Presidential_palace" title="Presidential palace">presidential palace</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Flagstaff_House" class="mw-redirect" title="The Flagstaff House">Flagstaff House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ahmadinejad_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmadinejad-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ahmadinejad2_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmadinejad2-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPP_welcomes_President_Ahmadinejad_visit_to_Ghana_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPP_welcomes_President_Ahmadinejad_visit_to_Ghana-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_welcomed_Iran's_President_Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_welcomed_Iran's_President_Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-President_Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-President_Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad-84">[84]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">Government of Ghana</a> reciprocated with an official <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visit</a> on 5 August 2013 by the <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_Ghana" title="Vice-President of Ghana">Vice-President of Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwesi_Amissah-Arthur" title="Kwesi Amissah-Arthur">Kwesi Amissah-Arthur</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Meeting" title="Meeting">met</a> with the Vice-President of Iran, <a href="/wiki/Eshaq_Jahangiri" title="Eshaq Jahangiri">Eshaq Jahangiri</a> on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Autarky" title="Autarky">autarky</a> and possible <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_trade" title="Bilateral trade">bilateral trade</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Republic of Iran">Islamic Republic of Iran</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Presidential_palace" title="Presidential palace">presidential palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sa%27dabad_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Sa'dabad Palace">Sa'dabad Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Iran_welcomes_expansion_of_trade_ties_with_Ghana:_Vice-president_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_welcomes_expansion_of_trade_ties_with_Ghana:_Vice-president-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UN_Agencies_in_Ghana">UN Agencies in Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: UN Agencies in Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>There are a number of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> Entities in the country such as the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">FAO</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Agricultural_Development" title="International Fund for Agricultural Development">IFAD</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organization" title="International Maritime Organization">IMO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_Compact_for_Migration" title="Global Compact for Migration">IOM</a>, <a href="/wiki/UN-HABITAT" class="mw-redirect" title="UN-HABITAT">UN-Habitat</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNAIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Capital_Development_Fund" title="United Nations Capital Development Fund">UNCDF</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">UNFPA</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UNHCR</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Information_Centres" title="United Nations Information Centres">UNIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Industrial_Development_Organization" title="United Nations Industrial Development Organization">UNIDO</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">UNODC</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_Project_Services" title="United Nations Office for Project Services">UNOPS</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">WFP</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainable_Development_Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sustainable Development Goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals_and_Ghana" title="Sustainable Development Goals and Ghana">Sustainable Development Goals and Ghana</a>
      </div>
      <p> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals_and_Ghana" title="Sustainable Development Goals and Ghana">Sustainable Development Goals in Ghana</a> were integrated into Ghana's development agenda and the budget. The SDGs were said to have been implemented through the decentralized planning system. This allows stakeholders participations such as UN Agencies, traditional leaders, civil society organizations, academia, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">SDGs</a> are a global call to action to end poverty among others. The goals are 17 in number and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> and its partners in the country are working towards achieving them.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>
      <p> According to the president <a href="/wiki/Nana_Akufo-Addo" title="Nana Akufo-Addo">Nana Akufo-Addo</a> of Ghana, Ghana was "the first <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan African">sub-Saharan African</a> country to achieve the goal of halving poverty, as contained in Goal 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>”<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_police">Law enforcement and police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Law enforcement and police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Ghana" title="Law enforcement in Ghana">Law enforcement in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg/220px-Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg/330px-Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="413" data-file-height="214"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Police_Service_Motorbikes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Militarized_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Militarized police">Militarized police</a> Unit of the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Police_Service" title="Ghana Police Service">Ghana Police Service</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Police_Service" title="Ghana Police Service">Ghana Police Service</a> (GPS) and the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department" title="Criminal Investigation Department">Criminal Investigation Department</a> (CID) are the main law enforcement agencies of the Republic of Ghana, and are responsible for the detection of crime, maintenance of law and order and the maintenance of internal peace and security.<sup id="cite_ref-MINT_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MINT-90">[90]</a></sup> The Ghana Police Service has eleven specialised police units including a <a href="/wiki/Militarized_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Militarized police">Militarized police</a> <a href="/wiki/Rapid_deployment_force" title="Rapid deployment force">Rapid deployment force</a> (RDF) and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Police_Service#Marine_Police_Unit" title="Ghana Police Service">Marine Police</a> Unit (MPU).<sup id="cite_ref-UNIT_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIT-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-POLICE_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POLICE-92">[92]</a></sup> The Ghana Police Service operates in 12 divisions: ten covering the ten regions of Ghana, one assigned specifically to the seaport and industrial hub of <a href="/wiki/Tema" title="Tema">Tema</a>, and the twelfth being the Railways, Ports and Harbours Division.<sup id="cite_ref-POLICE_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POLICE-92">[92]</a></sup> The Ghana Police Service's <a href="/wiki/Maritime_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime police">Marine Police</a> Unit and Division handles issues that arise from the country's offshore <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil and gas industry">oil and gas industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-POLICE_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POLICE-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Prisons_Service" title="Ghana Prisons Service">Ghana Prisons Service</a> and the sub-division <a href="/wiki/Borstal_Institute_for_Juveniles" title="Borstal Institute for Juveniles">Borstal Institute for Juveniles</a> administers <a href="/wiki/Incarceration" class="mw-redirect" title="Incarceration">incarceration</a> in Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Prisons_Service_General_Information_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Prisons_Service_General_Information-93">[93]</a></sup> Ghana retains and exercises the death penalty for treason, corruption, robbery, piracy, drug trafficking, rape, and homicide.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_Death_Penalty_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_Death_Penalty-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Criminal_Code_and_Courts_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Criminal_Code_and_Courts-95">[95]</a></sup> 27 convicts (all men) were sentenced to death in Ghana in 2012 and the Ghana Prisons Service statistics of the total number of convicts sentenced to death in Ghana as of December&nbsp;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> was 162 men and 4 women,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_Death_Penalty_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_Death_Penalty-94">[94]</a></sup> with a total prison inmate population of 13,983 convicts as of 22&nbsp;July&nbsp;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Prisons_Service_Inmate_Statistics_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Prisons_Service_Inmate_Statistics-96">[96]</a></sup> "The new sustainable development goals adopted by the United Nations call for the international community to come together to promote the rule of law; support equal access to justice for all; reduce corruption; and develop effective, accountable, and transparent institutions at all levels."<sup id="cite_ref-DIPNote:_Promoting_Peace,_Justice,_and_Strong_Institutions_in_the_Great_Lakes_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DIPNote:_Promoting_Peace,_Justice,_and_Strong_Institutions_in_the_Great_Lakes-97">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghanaian_drug_war_and_the_Narcotics_Control_Board">Ghanaian drug war and the Narcotics Control Board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ghanaian drug war and the Narcotics Control Board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Drugtrade.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Drugtrade.png/220px-Drugtrade.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Drugtrade.png/330px-Drugtrade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Drugtrade.png/440px-Drugtrade.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Drugtrade.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghana is among the sovereign states of West Africa used by <a href="/wiki/Drug_cartel" title="Drug cartel">drug cartels</a> and drug traffickers (shown in orange).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana is used as a key <a href="/wiki/Narcotic" title="Narcotic">narcotics</a> industry <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipment</a> point by traffickers, usually from South America as well as some from other African nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup> In 2013, the UN chief of the Office on Drugs and Crime (UNODC) stated that "West Africa is completely weak in terms of border control and the big drug cartels from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> have chosen Africa as a way to reach Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-DW_Made_for_minds:_Illegal_drug_use_on_the_rise_in_Africa_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW_Made_for_minds:_Illegal_drug_use_on_the_rise_in_Africa-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is not a wide or popular knowledge about the narcotics industry and intercepted narcotics within Ghana itself, due to the industry's operations and involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">underground economy</a>. The social context within which <a href="/wiki/Narcotic_trafficking" class="mw-redirect" title="Narcotic trafficking">narcotic trafficking</a>, storage, transportation, and repacking systems exist in Ghana and the state's location along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> within the Atlantic Ocean&nbsp;– only a few degrees north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>&nbsp;– makes Ghana an attractive country for the narcotics business.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Narcotics_Control_Board_(Ghana)" title="Narcotics Control Board (Ghana)">Narcotics Control Board</a> (NACOB) has impounded <a href="/wiki/Container_ship" title="Container ship">container ships</a> at the Sekondi Naval Base in the <a href="/wiki/Takoradi_Harbour" title="Takoradi Harbour">Takoradi Harbour</a>. These ships were carrying thousands of kilograms of cocaine, with a street value running into billions of <a href="/wiki/Ghana_cedi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghana cedi">Ghana cedis</a>. However, drug seizures saw a decline in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Drug_cartel" title="Drug cartel">Drug cartels</a> are using new methods in narcotics production and narcotics <a href="/wiki/Exportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Exportation">exportation</a>, to avoid Ghanaian security agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if-100">[100]</a></sup> Underdeveloped institutions, porous open borders, and the existence of established <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggling</a> organisations contribute to Ghana's position in the narcotics industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_could_be_taken_over_by_drug_barons_if-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Atta_Mills" title="John Atta Mills">John Atta Mills</a>, president between 2009 and 2012, initiated ongoing efforts to reduce the role of airports in Ghana's drug trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_hit_by_illegal_drug_trade-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Armed_Forces" title="Ghana Armed Forces">Ghana Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg/220px-Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg/330px-Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg/440px-Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Airforce_Reccep_Tayyip_Erdogan_Honor_Guard_at_Flagstaff_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkish_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish President">Turkish President</a> <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a> inspects <a href="/wiki/Guard_of_honour" title="Guard of honour">Honour Guards</a> mounted by the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Air_Force" title="Ghana Air Force">Ghana Air Force</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_House" title="Jubilee House">Jubilee House</a> the Presidential Palace of Ghana in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Accra_Region" title="Greater Accra Region">Greater Accra</a> on 1 March 2016.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1957, the Ghana Armed Forces (GAF) consisted of its headquarters, support services, three battalions of infantry and a reconnaissance squadron with armoured vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada's_Military_Assistance_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada's_Military_Assistance-101">[101]</a></sup> Ghanaian Prime Minister and President Kwame Nkrumah aimed at rapidly expanding the GAF to support the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Africa" title="United States of Africa">United States of Africa</a> ambitions. Thus in 1961, 4th and 5th Battalions were established, and in 1964 6th Battalion was established, from a <a href="/wiki/Paratrooper" title="Paratrooper">parachute</a> <a href="/wiki/Airborne_forces" title="Airborne forces">airborne unit</a> originally raised in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, Ghana is a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_hegemony" title="Regional hegemony">regional hegemon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-South_America_and_West_Africa_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_America_and_West_Africa-20">[20]</a></sup> In his book <i><a href="/wiki/Shake_Hands_with_the_Devil_(book)" title="Shake Hands with the Devil (book)">Shake Hands with the Devil</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> commander <a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A9o_Dallaire" title="Roméo Dallaire">Roméo Dallaire</a> highly rated the GAF soldiers and <a href="/wiki/Military_personnel" title="Military personnel">military personnel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada's_Military_Assistance_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada's_Military_Assistance-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">military operations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_doctrine" title="Military doctrine">military doctrine</a> of the GAF are conceptualised on the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ghana" title="Constitution of Ghana">Constitution of Ghana</a>, Ghana's Law on <a href="/wiki/Armed_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed Force">Armed Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_Strategy" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Strategy">Military Strategy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan_International_Peacekeeping_Training_Centre" title="Kofi Annan International Peacekeeping Training Centre">Kofi Annan International Peacekeeping Training Centre</a> (KAIPTC) agreements to which GAF is attestator.<sup id="cite_ref-Defence_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Defence-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana's_Regional_Security_Policy_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana's_Regional_Security_Policy-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KAIPTC_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KAIPTC-105">[105]</a></sup> GAF military operations are executed under the auspices and imperium of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Ghana)" title="Ministry of Defence (Ghana)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MoD) <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Defence_(Ghana)" title="Minister for Defence (Ghana)">Minister for Defence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Defence_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Defence-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vision_&amp;_Mission_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_&amp;_Mission-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although Ghana is relatively peaceful and is often considered to be one of the least violent countries in the region, Ghana has experienced political violence in the past and 2017 has thus far seen an upward trend in incidents motivated by political grievances.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Ghana signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Ghana" title="Administrative divisions of Ghana">Administrative divisions of Ghana</a>
      </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Ghana" title="Human rights in Ghana">Human rights in Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Ghana" title="LGBT rights in Ghana">LGBT rights in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexual acts</a> are prohibited by law in Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> According to 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 96% of Ghanaians believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-114">[114]</a></sup> Sometimes old <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Ghana" title="Women in Ghana">women in Ghana</a> are accused of <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>, particularly in rural Ghana. Issues of witchcraft mainly remain as speculations based on superstitions within families. In some parts of northern Ghana, there exists what are called <a href="/wiki/Witch_camp" title="Witch camp">witch camps</a>. This is said to house a total of around 1,000 people accused of witchcraft.<sup id="cite_ref-Camps_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camps-115">[115]</a></sup> The Ghanaian government has announced that it intends to close the camps.<sup id="cite_ref-Camps_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camps-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Ghana" title="Women in Ghana">women in Ghana</a> are given equal rights under the constitution of Ghana, disparities in education, employment, and healthcare for women remain prevalent. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ghana" title="Economy of Ghana">Economy of Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_media_in_Ghana" title="New media in Ghana">New media in Ghana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_Ghana#Automobile_manufacturing" title="Manufacturing in Ghana">Automobile manufacturing in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_sectors">Key sectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Key sectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg/220px-Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg/330px-Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg/440px-Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Export_Trends.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghana petroleum and <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">commodities</a>; exports in <a href="/wiki/Percentage" title="Percentage">percentage</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana is an average <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resource</a> enriched country possessing <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial minerals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Precious_metal" title="Precious metal">precious metals</a>. It is an emerging designated <a href="/wiki/Digital_economy" title="Digital economy">digital economy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> hybridisation and an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Emerging markets">emerging market</a> with 8.7% GDP growth in 2012. It has an <a href="/wiki/Economic_plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic plan">economic plan</a> target known as the "Ghana Vision 2020". This plan envisions Ghana as the first African country to become a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> between 2020 and 2029 and a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Newly industrialised country">newly industrialised country</a> between 2030 and 2039.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> This excludes fellow <a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">Group of 24</a> member and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> country South Africa, which is a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Newly industrialised country">newly industrialised country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Ghana's economy also has ties to the <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">Chinese yuan renminbi</a> along with Ghana's vast gold reserves. In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Ghana" title="Bank of Ghana">Bank of Ghana</a> began circulating the renminbi throughout Ghanaian state-owned banks and to the Ghana public as <a href="/wiki/Hard_currency" title="Hard currency">hard currency</a> along with the national <a href="/wiki/Ghana_cedi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghana cedi">Ghana cedi</a> for second national trade currency.<sup id="cite_ref-BoG_introduce_Chinese_Yuan_onto_the_FX_market_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoG_introduce_Chinese_Yuan_onto_the_FX_market-118">[118]</a></sup> Between 2012 and 2013, 37.9 percent of rural dwellers were experiencing poverty whereas only 10.6 percent of urban dwellers were.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Urban areas hold greater opportunity for employment, particularly in informal trade, while nearly all (94 percent) of rural poor households participate in the agricultural sector.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Volta_River_Authority" title="Volta River Authority">Volta River Authority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="Ghana National Petroleum Corporation">Ghana National Petroleum Corporation</a> are the two major electricity producers.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product-121">[121]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Akosombo_Dam" title="Akosombo Dam">Akosombo Dam</a>, built on the Volta River in 1965, along with <a href="/wiki/Bui_Dam" title="Bui Dam">Bui Dam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kpong_Dam" title="Kpong Dam">Kpong Dam</a>, and several other <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric dam">hydroelectric dams</a> provide hydropower.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_fuel_for_faster_development_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_fuel_for_faster_development-123">[123]</a></sup> In addition, the Government of Ghana has sought to <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Ghana" title="Nuclear energy in Ghana">build the second nuclear power plant in Africa</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Stock_Exchange" title="Ghana Stock Exchange">Ghana Stock Exchange</a> is the 5th largest on continental Africa and 3rd largest in sub-saharan Africa with a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Market capitalisation">market capitalisation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Cedi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghana Cedi">GH¢</a> 57.2&nbsp;billion or <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">CN¥</a> 180.4&nbsp;billion in 2012 with the South Africa <a href="/wiki/JSE_Limited" title="JSE Limited">JSE Limited</a> as first.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Stock_Exchange" title="Ghana Stock Exchange">Ghana Stock Exchange</a> (GSE) was the 2nd best performing <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> in sub-saharan Africa in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana also produces high-quality <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Entering_A_Sweet,_Golden_Era_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Entering_A_Sweet,_Golden_Era-126">[126]</a></sup> It is the 2nd largest producer of cocoa globally,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Entering_A_Sweet,_Golden_Era_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Entering_A_Sweet,_Golden_Era-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> and was projected to become the world's largest producer of cocoa in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_will_reclaim_top_spot_in_cocoa_production_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_will_reclaim_top_spot_in_cocoa_production-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana is classified as a middle income country.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertiary sector of industry">Services</a> account for 50% of GDP, followed by <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary sector of industry">manufacturing</a> (24.1%), <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary sector of industry">extractive industries</a> (5%), and taxes (20.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Ghana economy is an emerging digital-based mixed economy hybrid with an increasing primary manufacturing and export of digital technology goods along with assembling and exporting automobiles and ships, diverse resource rich exportation of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial minerals</a>, agricultural products primarily cocoa, petroleum and natural gas,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana's_Jubilee_oil_field_nears_output_plateau_-operator_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana's_Jubilee_oil_field_nears_output_plateau_-operator-130">[130]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Private_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Private industry">industries</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">information and communications technology</a> primarily via Ghana's state digital technology corporation <a href="/wiki/Rlg_Communications" title="Rlg Communications">Rlg Communications</a> which manufactures <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a> with <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> and various <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_Gross_Domestic_Product-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Top_5_Countries_for_ICT_in_Africa_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Top_5_Countries_for_ICT_in_Africa-131">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Urban_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban car">Urban</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> have been manufactured in Ghana since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Petroleum_and_natural_gas_production">Petroleum and natural gas production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Petroleum and natural gas production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_(GNPC)_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_%28GNPC%29_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png/220px-Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_%28GNPC%29_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_%28GNPC%29_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png/330px-Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_%28GNPC%29_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_%28GNPC%29_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png 2x" data-file-width="379" data-file-height="210"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jubilee_Oil_Field_of_the_Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation_(GNPC)_and_National_Petroleum_Authority.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jubilee_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Jubilee oil field">Jubilee oil field</a> of the Ghana National Petroleum Corporation (GNPC) and <a href="/wiki/National_Petroleum_Authority" title="National Petroleum Authority">National Petroleum Authority</a> located off the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Region_(Ghana)" title="Western Region (Ghana)">Western Region</a> in Ghana in the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="South Atlantic Ocean">South Atlantic Ocean</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana produces and exports an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbons</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sweet_crude_oil" title="Sweet crude oil">sweet crude oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Five_Countries_to_Watch_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Five_Countries_to_Watch-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The 100% state-owned <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">filling station</a> company of Ghana, <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Oil_Company" title="Ghana Oil Company">Ghana Oil Company</a> (GOIL) is the number 1 petroleum and gas filling station of Ghana and the 100% state-owned state oil company <a href="/wiki/Ghana_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="Ghana National Petroleum Corporation">Ghana National Petroleum Corporation</a> (GNPC) oversees <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">hydrocarbon exploration</a> and production of Ghana's entire petroleum and natural gas reserves. Ghana aims to further increase output of oil to 2.2&nbsp;million barrels (350,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) per day and gas to 34,000,000 cubic metres (1.2<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>9</sup>&nbsp;cu&nbsp;ft) per day.<sup id="cite_ref-cs2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs2-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Jubilee oil field">Jubilee Oilfield</a> which contains up to 3 billion barrels (480,000,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Sweet_crude_oil" title="Sweet crude oil">sweet crude oil</a> was discovered in 2007, among the many other offshore and inland oilfields in Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Ghana is believed to have up to 5 billion barrels (790,000,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) to 7 billion barrels (1.1<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup>&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of petroleum in reserves,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> which is the fifth largest in Africa and the 21st to 25th <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">largest proven reserves</a> in the world. It also has up to 1.7<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>11</sup> cubic metres (6<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>12</sup>&nbsp;cu&nbsp;ft) of natural gas in reserves,<sup id="cite_ref-Atuabo_gas_project_to_propel_more_growth_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atuabo_gas_project_to_propel_more_growth-139">[139]</a></sup> which is the sixth largest in Africa and the 49th <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">largest natural gas proven reserves</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil and gas exploration">Oil and gas exploration</a> off Ghana's eastern coast on the Gulf of Guinea is ongoing, and the amount of both crude oil and natural gas continues to increase. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">Government of Ghana</a> has drawn up plans to <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalise</a> Ghana's entire petroleum and natural gas reserves to increase government revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="box-Confusing plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-confusing" role="presentation">
