      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_minerals_mining">Industrial minerals mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Industrial minerals mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Ghana" title="Mining industry of Ghana">Mining industry of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Known for its <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial minerals</a>, Ghana is the world's 7th largest producer of gold, producing 130 <a href="/wiki/Metric_ton" class="mw-redirect" title="Metric ton">metric tons</a> in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-CEIC_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEIC-141">[141]</a></sup> and is now the largest producer in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> ahead of South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-CEIC_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEIC-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Ghana has the 9th largest reserves and the 9th largest production rate of diamonds in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">Industrial minerals</a> and exports from South Ghana include gold, silver, timber, diamonds, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>. South Ghana also has mineral deposits of <a href="/wiki/Barite" class="mw-redirect" title="Barite">barite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clay_minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Clay minerals">clay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolomite_(mineral)" title="Dolomite (mineral)">dolomite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feldspar" title="Feldspar">feldspar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, iron ore, <a href="/wiki/Kaolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaolin">kaolin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laterite" title="Laterite">laterite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesite" title="Magnesite">magnesite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mica" title="Mica">mica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">phosphorus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rocks</a>, salts, <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a>, silver, <a href="/wiki/Slate" title="Slate">slate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talc" title="Talc">talc</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> that are yet to be fully <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_natural_resources" title="Exploitation of natural resources">exploited</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The Government of Ghana has drawn up plans to <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalize</a> Ghana's entire mining industry to increase government revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_estate">Real estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Real estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_Villa_House_(South_Ghana).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg/220px-Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg/330px-Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg/440px-Luxury_Villa_House_%28South_Ghana%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_Villa_House_(South_Ghana).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Villa" title="Villa">villa</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Ridge,_Accra" title="East Ridge, Accra">East Ridge</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The real estate and <a href="/wiki/Housing_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Housing market">housing market</a> of Ghana has become an important and strategic <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">economic sector</a>, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Urban_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban centre">urban centres</a> of south Ghana such as Accra, Kumasi, Sekondi-Takoradi and Tema.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Property_market_faces_brighter_growth_prospects_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Property_market_faces_brighter_growth_prospects-148">[148]</a></sup> However, many of its citizens particularly those in Accra cannot afford the housing prices which is a trait of most major cities globally particularly in the West. Kumasi is growing at a faster rate than Accra, and there is less competition in its real estate market.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup> The gross rental <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> of Ghana is withheld at 10%, <a href="/wiki/Capital_gain" title="Capital gain">capital gains</a> are taxed at 15% with a 5% <a href="/wiki/Gift_tax" title="Gift tax">gift tax</a> imposed on the transfer of properties and Ghana's <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Real estate market">real estate market</a> is divided into 3 areas: public sector real estate development, emerging private sector real estate development, and private individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup> The activities of these 3 groups are facilitated by the Ghanaian banks and the primary mortgage market which has demonstrated enormous growth potential.<sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup> Recent developments in the Ghanaian economy has given birth to a boom in the construction sector, including the housing and public housing sector generating and injecting billions of dollars annually into the Ghanaian economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup> The real estate market investment perspective and attraction comes from Ghana's tropical location and robust political stability.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup> An increasing number of the Ghanaian populace are investing in properties and the Ghana government is empowering the <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> in the real estate direction.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Update_146-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Update-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana_147-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Estate_Market_in_Ghana-147">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_and_exports">Trade and exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Trade and exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_economy_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Ghana_economy_treemap.png/220px-Ghana_economy_treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Ghana_economy_treemap.png/330px-Ghana_economy_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Ghana_economy_treemap.png/440px-Ghana_economy_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="2393" data-file-height="1231"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_economy_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghana Export Treemap by Product (2017) from Harvard Atlas of Economic Complexity<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In July 2013, <a href="/wiki/International_Enterprise_Singapore" title="International Enterprise Singapore">International Enterprise Singapore</a> opened its 38th global office in Accra, to develop trade and investment on logistics, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transportation</a> and consumer sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana-150">[150]</a></sup> Singapore and Ghana also signed four bilateral agreements to promote <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> and <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> collaboration, as Ghana aims to predominantly shift its economic trade partnership to East Asia and Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana-150">[150]</a></sup> The economic centre is <a href="/wiki/International_Enterprise_Singapore" title="International Enterprise Singapore">IE Singapore</a>'s second office in Africa, coming six months after opening in Johannesburg, South Africa in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IE_Singapore_opens_office_in_Ghana-150">[150]</a></sup> Ghana's labour force in 2008 totalled 11.5&nbsp;million Ghanaian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-afdb_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afdb-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tema_Harbour" title="Tema Harbour">Tema Harbour</a> is Africa's largest <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/manmade" class="extiw" title="wikt:manmade">manmade</a> harbour and <a href="/wiki/Takoradi_Harbour" title="Takoradi Harbour">Takoradi Harbour</a> along with Tema harbour in Ghana handles goods and exports for Ghana. They are also traffic junctions where goods are transhipped; the Tema harbour handles the majority of the nation's export cargo and most of the country's chief exports is shipped from Takoradi harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-GPHA-Sekond-Takoradi_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPHA-Sekond-Takoradi-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GPHA-Tema_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPHA-Tema-154">[154]</a></sup> The Takoradi harbour and Tema harbour are operated by the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Ports_and_Harbours_Authority" title="Ghana Ports and Harbours Authority">Ghana Ports and Harbours Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GPHA-Sekond-Takoradi_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPHA-Sekond-Takoradi-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GPHA-Tema_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPHA-Tema-154">[154]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity_generation_sector">Electricity generation sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Electricity generation sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Ghana" title="Electricity sector in Ghana">Electricity sector in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Severe shortages of electricity in 2015 &amp; 2016 led to <a href="/wiki/Dumsor" title="Dumsor">dumsor</a> (persistent, irregular and unpredictable electric power outages),<sup id="cite_ref-germany_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany-155">[155]</a></sup> increasing the interest in renewables.<sup id="cite_ref-graphic1_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graphic1-156">[156]</a></sup> As of 2019, there is now a surplus of electricity which now presents a new set of financial challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_transparency">Economic transparency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economic transparency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to Transparency International's Corruption Perception Index of 2018, out of 180 countries, Ghana was ranked 78th, with a score of 41 on a scale where a 0–9 score means highly corrupt, and a 90–100 score means very clean. This was based on perceived levels of public sector corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, out of 177 countries, Ghana was ranked 63rd with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> with a score of 46.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Previously in 2012, the country ranked 64 and scored 45. Thus, Ghana's public sector scored lower in 2013 than in 2012, according to CPI's scores. </p>
      <p>Local reports have claimed that Ghana loses US$4.5&nbsp;billion annually from <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal gross domestic product</a> (Nominal GDP) growth as a result of economic corruption and economic crime by the incumbent <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Ghana)" title="National Democratic Congress (Ghana)">National Democratic Congress</a> (NDC) <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">government of Ghana</a> led by <a href="/wiki/John_Dramani_Mahama" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dramani Mahama">John Dramani Mahama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Loses_$4b_Annually_To_Corruption_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Loses_$4b_Annually_To_Corruption-160">[160]</a></sup> It is also said Ghana has lost an additional US$2.5&nbsp;billion from <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal gross domestic product</a> (Nominal GDP) growth between the months of January 2013 to October 2013 through economic corrupt practices under the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mahama_government_ministers" title="List of Mahama government ministers">Mahama administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Impeach_Mahama_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Impeach_Mahama-161">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The incumbent president is however seen to be fighting corruption by some government members,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and a fellow politician of an opposition party,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> after ordering investigations into scandals. Nonetheless others believe his actions are not sufficient in some cases.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/John_Addo_Kufuor" title="John Addo Kufuor">John Addo Kufuor</a>, son of former President <a href="/wiki/John_Agyekum_Kufuor" class="mw-redirect" title="John Agyekum Kufuor">John Agyekum Kufuor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kojo_Annan" title="Kojo Annan">Kojo Annan</a>, son of former Secretary-General of the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, have been named in association with the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Ghana was the first sub-Saharan African country to launch a cellular mobile network (1992). It was one of the first countries in Africa to be connected to the internet and to introduce ADSL broadband services.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaweb_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaweb-166">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_and_satellite_programmes">Space and satellite programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Space and satellite programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Space_Science_and_Technology_Centre" title="Ghana Space Science and Technology Centre">Ghana Space Science and Technology Centre</a> (GSSTC) and Ghana Space Agency (GhsA) oversee the <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Space program">space programmes</a> of Ghana. GSSTC and GhsA worked to have a <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">national security</a> <a href="/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite" title="Earth observation satellite">observational satellite</a> launched into orbit in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSpace_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSpace-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The first practical step in its endeavor was a <a href="/wiki/CanSat" title="CanSat">CanSat</a> launched on 15 May 2013, a space programme spearheaded by the All Nations University College (ANUC) in Koforidua. The CanSat was deployed 200 metres (660 feet) high from a helium-filled balloon and took some aerial images as well as temperature readings. As its next step in advancing space science and satellite technology in the sub-region, an amateur ground station has been designed and built by the university. It has successfully tracked and communicated with several (amateur) radio satellites in orbit including the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>, receiving <a href="/wiki/Slow-scan_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Slow-scan TV">slow-scan TV</a> images on 18 and 20 December 2014. The miniaturized earth observational satellite is to be launched into orbit in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-VOASpace_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOASpace-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's annual space exploration expenditure has been 1% of its gross domestic product (GDP), to support research in science and technology. In 2012, Ghana was elected to chair the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Science_and_Technology_for_Sustainable_Development_in_the_South" title="Commission on Science and Technology for Sustainable Development in the South">Commission on Science and Technology for Sustainable Development in the South</a> (Comsats); Ghana has a joint effort in <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> with South Africa's <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Space_Agency" title="South African National Space Agency">South African National Space Agency</a> (SANSA).<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSpace_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSpace-167">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cybernetics_and_cyberwarfare">Cybernetics and cyberwarfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cybernetics and cyberwarfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Sakawa" title="Sakawa">Sakawa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg/220px-Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg/330px-Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg/440px-Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Outreach_in_Ghana_6.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ghana" title="Education in Ghana">Ghana education system's</a> implementation of <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">information and communications technology</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ghana" title="University of Ghana">University of Ghana</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The use of computer technology for teaching and learning began to receive <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">government of Ghana</a>'s attention from the late 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report-170">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">information and communications technology</a> in education policy of Ghana requires the use of information and communications technology for teaching and learning at all levels of the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ghana" title="Education in Ghana">education of Ghana</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report-170">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Ghana)" title="Ministry of Education (Ghana)">Ministry of Education</a> (MOE) supports institutions in teaching of information and communications technology literacy.<sup id="cite_ref-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report_170-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report-170">[170]</a></sup> The majority of secondary, and some basic <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Ghana" title="List of schools in Ghana">schools of Ghana</a> have computer laboratories.<sup id="cite_ref-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report_170-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedagogical_Integration_of_ICT:_Ghana_Report-170">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's intention to become the information technology hub of West Africa has led the government of Ghana to enact cyber crime legislation and enhance <a href="/wiki/Cyber_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber security">cyber security</a> practices.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities-171">[171]</a></sup> Acting on that goal, in 2008 Ghana passed the <i>Electronic Communications Act</i> and the <i>Electronic Transactions Act</i>, which established the legal framework for governing information technology.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities-171">[171]</a></sup> In November 2011, the Deputy <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Communications_(Ghana)" title="Minister for Communications (Ghana)">Minister for Communications</a> and Technology announced the development of a national cyber security strategy, aimed at combating <a href="/wiki/Cyber_crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber crime">cyber crime</a> and securing critical infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2012, the <a href="/wiki/National_Information_Technology_Agency" title="National Information Technology Agency">National Information Technology Agency</a> (NITA) announced a national <a href="/wiki/Computer_emergency_response_team" title="Computer emergency response team">computer emergency response team</a> "strategy" designed to co-ordinate government response to cyberattacks, both internal and external.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities_171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities-171">[171]</a></sup> The agency also established <a href="/wiki/Computer_emergency_response_team" title="Computer emergency response team">computer emergency response teams</a> for each <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Ghana" title="Districts of Ghana">municipal, metropolitan, and district assembly</a> to improve co-ordination and information-sharing on <a href="/wiki/Threat_(computer)" title="Threat (computer)">cyberspace threats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities_171-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cyber_Index_–_International_Security_Trends_and_Realities-171">[171]</a></sup> Ghana is ranked 2nd on continental Africa and 7th globally in <a href="/wiki/Cyber_warfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber warfare">cyber warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyberterrorism" title="Cyberterrorism">cyberterrorism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyber_crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber crime">cyber crime</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Internet_crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet crime">internet crime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_biotechnology">Health and biotechnology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Health and biotechnology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Scientific_Research_into_Plant_Medicine" title="Centre for Scientific Research into Plant Medicine">Centre for Scientific Research into Plant Medicine</a> is an agency of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Ghana)" title="Ministry of Health (Ghana)">Ministry of Health</a> that was set up in the 1970s for both <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">R&amp;D</a> and as a practical resource (product production &amp; distribution/provision) primarily in areas of <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> related to <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">medicinal plants</a>. This includes both <a href="/wiki/Herbalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbalism">herbal medicine</a> and work on more advanced applications. It also has a secondary role as an educational resource for foreign students in health, biotechnology and related fields. </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ghana" title="Education in Ghana">Education in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Ghanaian education system is divided in three parts: Basic Education, secondary cycle, and tertiary education. "Basic Education" lasts 11 years (ages 4‒15).<sup id="cite_ref-GEScurr_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEScurr-173">[173]</a></sup> It is divided into <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">Kindergarten</a> (2 years), Primary School (2 modules of 3 years) and Junior High (3 years). Junior High School (JHS) ends with the Basic Education Certificate Examination (<a href="/wiki/BECE" class="mw-redirect" title="BECE">BECE</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-GEScurr_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEScurr-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GEScurr2_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEScurr2-174">[174]</a></sup> Once the BECE is achieved, the pupil can proceed to the secondary cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-BECE_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BECE-175">[175]</a></sup> Hence, the pupil has the choice between general education (offered by the Senior High School) and vocational education (offered by the technical Senior High School or the Technical and Vocational Institutes). Senior High School lasts three years and leads to the West African Secondary School Certificate Examination (<a href="/wiki/WASSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="WASSCE">WASSCE</a>), which is a prerequisite for enrollment in a university bachelor's degree programme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20137_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20137-176">[176]</a></sup> Polytechnics are open to vocational students, from SHS or TVI.<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-177">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A Bachelor's degree usually requires four years of study. It can be followed by a one- or two-year master's degree programme, which can be followed by a PhD programme of at least three years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20139_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20139-178">[178]</a></sup> A polytechnic programme lasts two or three years.<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-177">[177]</a></sup> Ghana also possesses numerous colleges of education.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Some of the notable universities in Ghana are The University of Ghana, Legon, Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology, and University of Cape Coast, just to mention a few.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The Ghanaian education system from kindergarten up to an undergraduate degree level generally takes 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The academic year usually goes from August to May inclusive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20134–5_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20134–5-182">[182]</a></sup> The school year in primary education lasts 40 weeks in Primary School and SHS and 45 weeks in JHS.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20135_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENUFFIC20135-183">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enrollment">Enrollment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Enrollment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:554px;max-width:554px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:275px;max-width:275px">

           <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png/273px-Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png" decoding="async" width="273" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png/410px-Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png/546px-Ghana_Ratio_of_Girls_to_Boys_in_Primary_and_Secondary_Education.png 2x" data-file-width="710" data-file-height="300"></a>

           Ratio of females to males in education system.
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:275px;max-width:275px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png/273px-Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png" decoding="async" width="273" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png/410px-Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png/546px-Ghana_Children_Out_Of_School.png 2x" data-file-width="710" data-file-height="300"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <center>
            Females and males out of education system.
           </center>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With over 95% of its children in school, Ghana currently has one of the highest school enrollment rates in all of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_–_Basic_Education_and_Gender_Equality_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF_–_Basic_Education_and_Gender_Equality-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The ratio of females to males in the total education system was 0.98, in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-news.myjoyonline.com_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.myjoyonline.com-186">[186]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_students">Foreign students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Foreign students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Ghana's education system annually attracts a large number of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_student" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign student">foreign students</a> particularly in the university sector.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding_of_education">Funding of education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Funding of education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The government largely funds basic education comprising public primary schools and public junior high schools. Senior high schools were subsidised by the government until September 2017/2018 academic year that senior high education became free.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> At the higher education level, the government funds more than 80% of resources provided to public universities, polytechnics and teacher training colleges. </p>
      <p>As part of the Free Compulsory Universal Basic Education, Fcube, the government supplies all basic education schools with all their textbooks and other educational supplies like exercise books. Senior high schools are also provided with all their textbook requirement by the government. Private schools acquire their educational material from private suppliers.<sup id="cite_ref-KoinzerNikolai2017_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KoinzerNikolai2017-190">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kindergarten_and_education_structure">Kindergarten and education structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Kindergarten and education structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Education_Structure.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ghana_Education_Structure.gif/220px-Ghana_Education_Structure.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ghana_Education_Structure.gif/330px-Ghana_Education_Structure.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ghana_Education_Structure.gif/440px-Ghana_Education_Structure.gif 2x" data-file-width="617" data-file-height="422"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Education_Structure.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <center>
          Education structure of Ghana
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The female and male ages 15–24 years literacy rate in Ghana was 81% in 2010, with males at 82%,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> and females at 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghanaian children begin their education at the age of three or four starting from <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> (nursery school and <a href="/wiki/Preschool" title="Preschool">preschool</a>), then to elementary school (primary school), high school (<a href="/wiki/Junior_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior high school">junior high school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senior_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior high school">senior high school</a>) and finally university. The average age at which a Ghanaian child enters primary school is 6 years.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_–_Basic_Education_and_Gender_Equality_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF_–_Basic_Education_and_Gender_Equality-184">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana has a <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> 6-year primary school education system beginning at age six,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Lauded_for_Free_Primary_School_Program_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Lauded_for_Free_Primary_School_Program-193">[193]</a></sup> and, under the educational reforms implemented in 1988 and reformed in 2007, they pass on to a 3-year junior high school system. At the end of the third year of junior high, there is a mandatory "<a href="/wiki/Basic_Education_Certificate_Examination" title="Basic Education Certificate Examination">Basic Education Certificate Examination</a>". Those continuing must complete the 4-year senior high school programme (which has been changed to three years) and take an admission exam to enter any university or tertiary programme. The Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Education_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Education system">education system</a> from nursery school up to an <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degree" title="Undergraduate degree">undergraduate degree</a> level takes 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005, Ghana had 12,130 primary schools, 5,450 junior secondary schools, 503 senior secondary schools, 21 public training colleges, 18 technical institutions, two diploma-awarding institutions and 6 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_in_Ghana_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Ghana-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nab.gov.gh_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nab.gov.gh-195">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010, there were relatively more females (53.0%) than males (40.5%) with primary school and JSS (junior secondary school) / JHS (<a href="/wiki/Junior_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior high school">junior high school</a>) as their highest level of education.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elementary">Elementary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Elementary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Ghana)" title="Ministry of Education (Ghana)">Ghanaian Ministry of Education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Accreditation_Board_(Ghana)" title="National Accreditation Board (Ghana)">Ghanaian National Accreditation Board</a> provide <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> at the elementary school (primary school) level, and most Ghanaians have relatively easy access to high school education (<a href="/wiki/Junior_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior high school">junior high school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senior_high_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior high school">senior high school</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Lauded_for_Free_Primary_School_Program_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Lauded_for_Free_Primary_School_Program-193">[193]</a></sup> These numbers can be contrasted with the single university and handful of secondary and primary schools that existed at the time of independence in 1957. Ghana's spending on education has varied between 28 and 40% of its annual budget in the past decade. All teaching is done in English, mostly by qualified Ghanaian educators.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> The courses taught at the primary or basic school level include English, Ghanaian language and culture, mathematics, environmental studies, social studies, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin</a> and French as an <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">OIF</a> associated-member,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> integrated or <a href="/wiki/General_science" class="mw-redirect" title="General science">general science</a>, pre-<a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational</a> skills and pre-<a href="/wiki/Technical_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical education">technical</a> skills, religious and moral education, and physical activities such as Ghanaian music and dance, and <a href="/wiki/Physical_education" title="Physical education">physical education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_school">High school</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: High school">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_senior_secondary_schools_in_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="List of senior secondary schools in Ghana">List of senior secondary schools in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The senior high level school curriculum has core subjects and elective subjects of which students must take four the core subjects of English language, mathematics, integrated science (including science, agriculture and environmental studies) and <a href="/wiki/Social_studies" title="Social studies">social studies</a> (economics, geography, history and government).<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>High school students also choose four elective subjects from five available programmes: agriculture programme, general programme (arts or science option), <a href="/wiki/Business_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Business program">business programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational</a> programme and <a href="/wiki/Technical_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical education">technical</a> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> Apart from most primary and secondary schools which choose the Ghanaian system of schooling, there are also international schools such as the <a href="/wiki/Takoradi_International_School" title="Takoradi International School">Takoradi International School</a>, Tema International School, <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_International_School,_Accra" title="Galaxy International School, Accra">Galaxy International School</a>, The Roman Ridge School, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Community_School" title="Lincoln Community School">Lincoln Community School</a>, Faith Montessori School, American International School, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Beta_Christian_College" title="Alpha Beta Christian College">Alpha Beta Christian College</a>, Ghana Christian International High School, Association International School, New Nation School, SOS Hermann Gmeiner International College, Vilac International School, <a href="/wiki/Akosombo_International_School" title="Akosombo International School">Akosombo International School</a> (which offers Cambridge O level certificate), North Legon Little Campus and International Community School, which offer the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureat" class="mw-redirect" title="International Baccalaureat">International Baccalaureat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Level_General_Certificate_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Level General Certificate of Education">Advanced Level General Certificate of Education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="International General Certificate of Secondary Education">International General Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (IGCSE).<sup id="cite_ref-Education_in_Ghana_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Ghana-194">[194]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University">University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Education,_Winneba_(UEW)_North_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg/200px-University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg/300px-University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg/400px-University_of_Education%2C_Winneba_%28UEW%29_North_Campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Front view of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Education,_Winneba" title="University of Education, Winneba">University of Education, Winneba</a> (UEW) North Campus in Winneba
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg/200px-Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg/300px-Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg/400px-Balme_Library_of_University_of_Ghana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1024"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Main entrance to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ghana" title="University of Ghana">University of Ghana</a>'s Balme Library in Accra
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Ghana" title="List of universities in Ghana">List of universities in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are eight national public universities in Ghana: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ghana" title="University of Ghana">University of Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology">Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cape_Coast" title="University of Cape Coast">University of Cape Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Education,_Winneba" title="University of Education, Winneba">University of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_for_Development_Studies" title="University for Development Studies">University for Development Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mines_and_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Mines and Technology">University of Mines and Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Professional_Studies,_Accra" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Professional Studies, Accra">University of Professional Studies, Accra</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Energy_and_Natural_Resources" title="University of Energy and Natural Resources">University of Energy and Natural Resources</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Health_and_Allied_Sciences" title="University of Health and Allied Sciences">University of Health and Allied Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana has a growing number of accredited private universities including <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_University,_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Lancaster University, Ghana">Lancaster University, Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Technology_University_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghana Technology University College">Ghana Technology University College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashesi_University_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashesi University College">Ashesi University College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodist_University_College_Ghana" title="Methodist University College Ghana">Methodist University College Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_University_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Central University College">Central University College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accra_Institute_of_Technology" title="Accra Institute of Technology">Accra Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regent_University_College_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Regent University College of Science and Technology">Regent University College of Science and Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valley_View_University" title="Valley View University">Valley View University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_University_College_of_Ghana" title="Catholic University College of Ghana">Catholic University College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_University_College" title="Presbyterian University College">Presbyterian University College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zenith_University_College" title="Zenith University College">Zenith University College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The oldest university in Ghana, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ghana" title="University of Ghana">University of Ghana</a>, was founded in 1948. It had 29,754 students in 2008. Its programmes in the arts, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>, business, and the <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social sciences</a>, as well as medicine, are among the best in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many universities—including <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>—have special study-abroad programmes with Ghanaian schools and provide their students the opportunity to study abroad at Ghanaian universities. <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> has a campus in Accra.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The University of Ghana has seen a shift of its traditionally best students to the <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology">Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Ghana_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Ghana-201">[201]</a></sup> Since Ghana's independence, the country has been one of the most educational in sub-Saharan Africa. Former UN Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> has been chancellor of the University of Ghana since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Ghana_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Ghana-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology, the second university to be established in the country, is the premier university of science and technology in Ghana and West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System_181-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Brief_History_of_the_Ghanaian_Educational_System-181">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Ghana" title="Demographics of Ghana">Demographics of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian people</a>
      </div>

         <td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">source:<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-203">[203]</a></sup></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ghana_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana is a <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic society">multiethnic country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census-2">[2]</a></sup> The largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_people" title="Ashanti people">Ashanti people</a>. Ghana's territorial area within West Africa was unoccupied and uninhabited by humans until the 10th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Historical_Geography_of_Ghana_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Historical_Geography_of_Ghana-204">[204]</a></sup> By the 10th century AD, the <a href="/wiki/Guang_people" title="Guang people">Guans</a> were the first settlers in Ghana long before the other tribes came. <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akans</a> had established <a href="/wiki/Bonoman" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonoman">Bonoman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brong-Ahafo_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brong-Ahafo Region">Brong Ahafo</a> region) and were joined by the current settlers and inhabitants by the 16th century. </p>
      <p>In 2010, the population of Ghana was 72.2% Christian (24.3% <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>, 18.4% <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, 13.1% <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> and 11.4% other). Approximately 18.6% of the population of Ghana are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_CIA_World_FactBook_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_CIA_World_FactBook-19">[19]</a></sup> (51% <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>, 16% <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a>, and 8% <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-religion2010_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2010-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pew_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-206">[206]</a></sup> Just over 10,000 Ghanaians practise Hinduism, with most of them being indigenous converts. Hinduism in Ghana was popularized by Swami Ghana Nanda ji, who opened several temples in the nation. The temple of Lord Shiva in Accra is one of the largest where there are celebrations to Ganesh Chaturthi, Rath Yatra, and other Hindu observations. </p>
      <p>The Bahá’í religious community, established in Ghana in 1951, today includes more than 100 communities and over 50 local Bahá’í administrative councils, called Local Spiritual Assemblies.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are 375,000 registered legal <a href="/wiki/Skilled_worker" title="Skilled worker">skilled workers</a> (permanent residents) or <a href="/wiki/Foreign_worker" title="Foreign worker">foreign workers</a>/students (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Card" title="Ghana Card">Ghana Card</a> holders) inhabitants with an annually 1.5&nbsp;million transited airport <a href="/wiki/Layover" title="Layover">layovers</a>. In its first post-colonial census in 1960, Ghana had a population of 6.7&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The median age of Ghanaian citizens is 30 years old and the average household size is 3.6 persons. The Government of Ghana states that the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Ghana is English,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Ghanaian_Government_states_that_English_is_the_official_language_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Ghanaian_Government_states_that_English_is_the_official_language-1">[1]</a></sup> and is spoken by 67.1% of the inhabiting population of Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_–_2010_Population_and_Housing_Census-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Immigration_Service" title="Ghana Immigration Service">Ghana Immigration Service</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_nationality_law" title="Ghanaian nationality law">Ghanaian nationality law</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg/220px-Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg/330px-Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg/440px-Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Card_biometric.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ghana_Card" title="Ghana Card">Ghana Card</a> (Ghanaian electronic ID Card) – obverse with <a href="/wiki/Biometric_passport" title="Biometric passport">chip</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 22&nbsp;June&nbsp;2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ghana has a population of 30,083,000.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Around 29 percent of the population is under the age of 15, while persons aged 15–64 make up 57.8 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-databank.worldbank.org_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-databank.worldbank.org-210">[210]</a></sup> The Ashanti Region had the most, (<a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Ashanti_people" title="Ashanti people">Ashanti</a>) (4.7&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Region" title="Ashanti Region">Ashanti</a>, 2.3&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Brong-Ahafo_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brong-Ahafo Region">Brong-Ahafo</a>, 2.2&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Central_Region_(Ghana)" title="Central Region (Ghana)">Central</a>, 2.6&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Region_(Ghana)" title="Eastern Region (Ghana)">Eastern</a>, 2.3&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Western_Region_(Ghana)" title="Western Region (Ghana)">Western</a>, and 4&nbsp;million in the <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_government" title="Seat of government">seat of government</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Accra_Region" title="Greater Accra Region">Greater Accra</a> geographically and legally part of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Region_(Ghana)" title="Eastern Region (Ghana)">Eastern</a> then administered separately on 23 July 1982).<sup id="cite_ref-religion2010_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2010-205">[205]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 4.1&nbsp;million persons reside in the Northern territories (2.4&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Region_(Ghana)" title="Northern Region (Ghana)">Northern</a>, 1&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Region" title="Upper East Region">Upper East</a>, and 0.7&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Upper_West_Region" title="Upper West Region">Upper West</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-religion2010_205-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2010-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 2.1&nbsp;million persons reside in <a href="/wiki/Ewe_people" title="Ewe people">Ewe</a> territory <a href="/wiki/Volta_Region" title="Volta Region">Volta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-religion2010_205-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2010-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Ghana" title="Immigration to Ghana">Immigration to Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigration in Ghana">Illegal immigration in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to the recent legal immigration of <a href="/wiki/Skilled_worker" title="Skilled worker">skilled workers</a> who possess <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Card" title="Ghana Card">Ghana Cards</a>, there is a small population of Chinese, Malaysian, Indian, Middle Eastern and European nationals. </p>
      <p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Immigration_Service" title="Ghana Immigration Service">Ghana Immigration Service</a> reported a large number of <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrant" title="Economic migrant">economic migrants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigrant">Illegal immigrants</a> inhabiting Ghana: 14.6% (or 3.1&nbsp;million) of Ghana's 2010 population (predominantly <a href="/wiki/Nigerians" title="Nigerians">Nigerians</a>, Burkinabe citizens, Togolese citizens, and Malian citizens). In 1969, under the "Ghana Aliens Compliance Order" (GACO) <a href="/wiki/Enactment_of_a_bill" class="mw-redirect" title="Enactment of a bill">enacted</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ghana" title="Prime Minister of Ghana">Prime Minister of Ghana</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Abrefa_Busia" title="Kofi Abrefa Busia">Kofi Abrefa Busia</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Owes_no_Apology_to_Anybody_for_Aliens_Compliance_Order_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Owes_no_Apology_to_Anybody_for_Aliens_Compliance_Order-211">[211]</a></sup> Government of Ghana with BGU (<a href="/wiki/Border_Guard_Unit" title="Border Guard Unit">Border Guard Unit</a>) <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deported</a> over 3,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">aliens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigrant">illegal immigrants</a> in three months as they made up 20% of the population at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Owes_no_Apology_to_Anybody_for_Aliens_Compliance_Order_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Owes_no_Apology_to_Anybody_for_Aliens_Compliance_Order-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_History_of_Ghana's_1969_Aliens_Compliance_Order_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_History_of_Ghana's_1969_Aliens_Compliance_Order-212">[212]</a></sup> In 2013, there was a mass deportation of illegal miners, more than 4,000 of them Chinese nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Ghana" title="Languages of Ghana">Languages of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Akan_Greetings_(Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome;_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG/220px-Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG/330px-Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG/440px-Akan_Greetings_%28Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome%3B_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="880" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Akan_Greetings_(Akwaba_%E2%80%93_Welcome;_Ete_sen_%E2%80%93_Hello).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ashanti <a href="/wiki/Greeting" title="Greeting">greeting</a> <a href="/wiki/Phrase" title="Phrase">phrases</a>; "akɔaba" (welcome) and "ɛte sɛn" (how is it?) in Ashanti Twi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>English is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USA_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Additionally, there are eleven languages that have the status of government-sponsored languages: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ga_language" title="Ga language">Ga</a></li> 
       <li>four <a href="/wiki/Akan_language" title="Akan language">Akan languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Asante_dialect" title="Asante dialect">Asante Twi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akuapem_Twi" class="mw-redirect" title="Akuapem Twi">Akuapem Twi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fante_dialect" title="Fante dialect">Fante</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nzema_language" title="Nzema language">Nzema</a>)</li> 
       <li>two <a href="/wiki/Oti-Volta_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Oti-Volta languages">Mole-Dagbani ethnic</a> languages (<a href="/wiki/Dagaare" class="mw-redirect" title="Dagaare">Dagaare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dagomba_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dagomba language">Dagbanli</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ewe_language" title="Ewe language">Ewe</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Adangme_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Adangme language">Dangme</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Guan_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guan language">Guan</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kasem_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kasem language">Kasem</a><sup id="cite_ref-NCA_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCA-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Of these, <a href="/wiki/Akan_language" title="Akan language">Akan</a> is the most widely spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-Introduction_To_The_Verbal_and_Multi-Verbalsystem_of_Akan_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_To_The_Verbal_and_Multi-Verbalsystem_of_Akan-219">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to Ghana being surrounded by <a href="/wiki/French-speaking_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="French-speaking countries">French-speaking countries</a>, French is widely taught in schools and universities, as well as a language used for commercial and international economic exchanges and is spoken in some regions. Since 2006, Ghana has been an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> the global organisation that unites French-speaking countries (84 nations on 6 continents). In 2005, over 350 000 Ghanaian children studied French in schools. Since then, its status has progressively been updated to a mandatory language in every high school.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> It is the process of becoming an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_Pidgin_English" title="Ghanaian Pidgin English">Ghanaian Pidgin English</a> (GhPE), also known as Kru English (or, in <a href="/wiki/Akan_language" title="Akan language">Akan</a>, <i>kroo brofo</i>), is a variety of <a href="/wiki/West_African_Pidgin_English" title="West African Pidgin English">West African Pidgin English</a> spoken mainly in Accra and in the southern towns.<sup id="cite_ref-Huber_1999_p139_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huber_1999_p139-224">[224]</a></sup> GhPE can be divided into two varieties, referred to as "uneducated" or "non-institutionalized" pidgin and "educated" or "institutionalized" pidgin, the former associated with uneducated or illiterate people and the latter acquired and used in institutions such as universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Huber_1999_p138-153_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huber_1999_p138-153-225">[225]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
