      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <p>Ghana is a largely Christian country, although a sizable Muslim minority exists. Traditional (indigenous) beliefs are also practised. </p>
      <p><br> The fertility rate of Ghana declined from 3.99 (2000) to 3.28 (2010) with 2.78 in urban region and 3.94 in rural region.<sup id="cite_ref-statsghana.gov.gh_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsghana.gov.gh-231">[228]</a></sup> The United Nations reports a fertility decline from 6.95 (1970) to 4.82 (2000) to 3.93 live births per woman in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[229]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortality">Mortality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Mortality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Life expectancy at birth in 2018 was 64 for a female and 62 for a male.<sup id="cite_ref-CDC_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDC-233">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The top ten causes of death in Ghana in 2018 were:<sup id="cite_ref-CDC_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDC-233">[230]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>Malaria</li> 
       <li>Lower respiratory infections</li> 
       <li>Neonatal disorders</li> 
       <li>Ischemic heart disease</li> 
       <li>Stroke</li> 
       <li>HIV/AIDS</li> 
       <li>Tuberculosis</li> 
       <li>Diarrheal diseases</li> 
       <li>Road injuries</li> 
       <li>Diabetes</li>
      </ol> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Ghana" title="Crime in Ghana">Crime in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Crime in Ghana is investigated by the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Police_Service" title="Ghana Police Service">Ghana Police Service</a>. Ghana had <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">a murder rate</a> of 1.68 per 100,000 population in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-UNODCnew_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNODCnew-234">[231]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universal_health_care_and_life_expectancy">Universal health care and life expectancy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Universal health care and life expectancy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Insurance_Scheme_(Ghana)" title="National Health Insurance Scheme (Ghana)">NHIS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Ghana" title="Health in Ghana">Health in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eye_care_in_Ghana" title="Eye care in Ghana">Eye care in Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Optometry_in_Ghana" title="Optometry in Ghana">Optometry in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana has a <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> system strictly designated for <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian nationals</a>, National Health Insurance Scheme (NHIS).<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[232]</a></sup> Health care is very variable throughout Ghana and in 2012, over 12&nbsp;million Ghanaian nationals were covered by the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Insurance_Scheme_(Ghana)" title="National Health Insurance Scheme (Ghana)">National Health Insurance Scheme (Ghana)</a> (NHIS).<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_National_Health_Insurance_Scheme_(NHIS)_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_National_Health_Insurance_Scheme_(NHIS)-236">[233]</a></sup> Urban centres are well served, and contain most of the hospitals, clinics, and pharmacies in Ghana. There are over 200 hospitals in Ghana and Ghana is a destination for <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[234]</a></sup> In 2010, there were 0.1 physicians per 1,000 people and as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 0.9 hospital beds per 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-databank.worldbank.org_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-databank.worldbank.org-210">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2014 estimate of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> at birth had increased to an average of 65.75 years with males at 63.4 years and females at 68.2 years,<sup id="cite_ref-CIAlife2013_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAlife2013-238">[235]</a></sup> and in 2013 <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> decreased to 39 per 1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-Listing:_Infant_mortality_rate_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Listing:_Infant_mortality_rate-239">[236]</a></sup> Sources vary on life expectancy at birth; the World Health Organization (WHO) estimated 62 years for men and 64 years for women born in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[237]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There was an estimation of 15 physicians and 93 nurses per 100,000 persons in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-241">[238]</a></sup> 5.2% of Ghana's GDP was spent on health in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Field_Listing:_Health_expenditures_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Field_Listing:_Health_expenditures-242">[239]</a></sup> and all <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian</a> <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizens</a> have the right to access <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" title="Primary health care">primary health care</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bill_Gates_Ghana_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill_Gates_Ghana-243">[240]</a></sup> In May 2020, the <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a> announced Ghana became the second country in the WHO African Region to attain regulatory system "maturity level 3", the second-highest in the four-tiered WHO classification of <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_medicines_regulatory_systems&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National medicines regulatory systems (page does not exist)">National medicines regulatory systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[241]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> prevalence was estimated at 1.40% among adults aged 15–49.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:right;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ghana" title="Culture of Ghana">Culture of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg/220px-FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg/330px-FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg/440px-FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FB_20151104_19_47_22_Saved_Picture(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hogbetsotso_festival" title="Hogbetsotso festival">Hogbetsotso festival</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Volta_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Volta region">Volta region</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghanaian culture is a diverse mixture of the practices and beliefs of many different <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian</a> ethnic groups. The 2010 census reported that the largest ethnic groups are the Akan (47.3 percent), the Mole-Dagbani (16.6 percent), the Ewe (13.9 percent), the Ga-Dangme (7.4 percent), the Gurma (5.7) and the Guan (3.7 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-statsghana.gov.gh_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsghana.gov.gh-231">[228]</a></sup> The Akan make up a majority of the population in the Central (81.7 percent), Western (78.2 percent), Ashanti (74.2 percent), Brong Ahafo (58.9 percent) and Eastern (51.1 percent) regions.<sup id="cite_ref-statsghana.gov.gh_231-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsghana.gov.gh-231">[228]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">Food and drink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Food and drink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_cuisine" title="Ghanaian cuisine">Ghanaian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_cuisine" title="Ghanaian cuisine">Ghanaian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a> is diverse, and includes an assortment of <a href="/wiki/Soup" title="Soup">soups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a> with varied seafoods and most Ghanaian soups are prepared with vegetables, meat, poultry or fish.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> Fish is important in the Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Diet_(nutrition)" title="Diet (nutrition)">diet</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">tilapia</a>, roasted and fried <a href="/wiki/Whitebait" title="Whitebait">whitebait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smoked_fish" title="Smoked fish">smoked fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crayfish" title="Crayfish">crayfish</a> all being common components of Ghanaian dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Banku" title="Banku">Banku</a> (<a href="/wiki/Akple" title="Akple">akple</a>) is a common Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Starch" title="Starch">starchy</a> food made from ground corn (maize),<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> and cornmeal based staples, kɔmi (<a href="/wiki/Kenkey" title="Kenkey">kenkey</a>) and banku (akple) are usually accompanied by some form of <a href="/wiki/Fried_fish" title="Fried fish">fried fish</a> (chinam) or grilled tilapia and a very spicy condiment made from raw red and green <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chillies</a>, onions and tomatoes (<a href="/wiki/Pepper_sauce" class="mw-redirect" title="Pepper sauce">pepper sauce</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> Banku and tilapia is a combo served in most Ghanaian restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">Fufu</a> is the most common exported Ghanaian dish, in that it is a delicacy across the <a href="/wiki/African_diaspora" title="African diaspora">African diaspora</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup_246-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_cuisine,_banku,_okra_and_soup-246">[243]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Ghanaian national literature radio programme and accompanying publication <i><a href="/wiki/Voices_of_Ghana" title="Voices of Ghana">Voices of Ghana</a></i> was one of the earliest on the African continent. The most prominent Ghanaian authors are novelists; <a href="/wiki/J._E._Casely_Hayford" title="J. E. Casely Hayford">J. E. Casely Hayford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayi_Kwei_Armah" title="Ayi Kwei Armah">Ayi Kwei Armah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nii_Ayikwei_Parkes" class="mw-redirect" title="Nii Ayikwei Parkes">Nii Ayikwei Parkes</a>, who gained international acclaim with the books, <i><a href="/wiki/Ethiopia_Unbound" title="Ethiopia Unbound">Ethiopia Unbound</a></i> (1911), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beautyful_Ones_Are_Not_Yet_Born" title="The Beautyful Ones Are Not Yet Born">The Beautyful Ones Are Not Yet Born</a></i> (1968) and <i>Tail of the Blue Bird</i> (2009), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-LIT_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIT-247">[244]</a></sup> In addition to novels, other literature arts such as Ghanaian theatre and poetry have also had a very good development and support at the national level with prominent Ghanaian playwrights and poets <a href="/wiki/Joe_de_Graft" title="Joe de Graft">Joe de Graft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Efua_Sutherland" title="Efua Sutherland">Efua Sutherland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LIT_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIT-247">[244]</a></sup> Much of the 2016 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Homegoing_(Gyasi_novel)" title="Homegoing (Gyasi novel)">Homegoing</a></i> by Ghanaian-born American writer <a href="/wiki/Yaa_Gyasi" title="Yaa Gyasi">Yaa Gyasi</a> takes place in Ghana. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adinkra">Adinkra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Adinkra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adinkra_symbols" title="Adinkra symbols">Adinkra symbols</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg/220px-Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg/330px-Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="214"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Adinkra_motifs_Rattray_1927.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Adinkra_symbols" title="Adinkra symbols">Adinkra symbols</a> by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Sutherland_Rattray" title="Robert Sutherland Rattray">Robert Sutherland Rattray</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the 13th century, Ghanaians developed their unique art of <i><a href="/wiki/Adinkra_symbols" title="Adinkra symbols">adinkra</a></i> printing. Hand-printed and hand-<a href="/wiki/Embroidery" title="Embroidery">embroidered</a> adinkra clothes were made and used exclusively by the then Ghanaian royalty for devotional ceremonies. Each of the <a href="/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)" title="Motif (visual arts)">motifs</a> that make up the <a href="/wiki/Text_corpus" title="Text corpus">corpus</a> of adinkra symbolism has a name and meaning derived from a proverb, a historical event, human attitude, <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">ethology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plant_life-form" title="Plant life-form">plant life-form</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Shape" title="Shape">shapes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Inanimate" class="mw-redirect" title="Inanimate">inanimate</a> and man-made objects. These are graphically rendered in stylised geometric shapes. The meanings of the motifs may be categorised into <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics" title="Aesthetics">aesthetics</a>, ethics, <a href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationship" title="Interpersonal relationship">human relations</a>, and concepts.<sup id="cite_ref-LIT_247-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIT-247">[244]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Adinkra symbols have a decorative function as tattoos but also represent objects that encapsulate evocative messages that convey traditional wisdom, aspects of life or the environment. There are many different symbols with distinct meanings, often linked with <a href="/wiki/Proverb" title="Proverb">proverbs</a>. In the words of <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Appiah" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony Appiah">Anthony Appiah</a>, they were one of the means in a pre-literate society for "supporting the transmission of a complex and nuanced body of practice and belief".<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[245]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_clothing">Traditional clothing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Traditional clothing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kente_cloth" title="Kente cloth">Kente cloth</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kent_wove.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg/220px-Kent_wove.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg/330px-Kent_wove.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg 2x" data-file-width="371" data-file-height="513"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kent_wove.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kente cloth, the traditional or national cloth of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Ghana</a>, is worn by most southern Ghanaian ethnic groups including the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ga-Adangbe_people" title="Ga-Adangbe people">Ga</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ewe_people" title="Ewe people">Ewe</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Along with the <i>Adinkra cloth</i> Ghanaians use many different cloth fabrics for their traditional attire.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> The different ethnic groups have their own individual cloth. The most well known is the <a href="/wiki/Kente" class="mw-redirect" title="Kente">Kente</a> cloth.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> Kente is a very important Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/National_costume" class="mw-redirect" title="National costume">national costume</a> and clothing and these cloths are used to make traditional and modern Ghanaian Kente <a href="/wiki/Attire" class="mw-redirect" title="Attire">attire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Different symbols and different colours mean different things.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kente_cloth" title="Kente cloth">Kente</a> is the most famous of all the Ghanaian cloths.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> Kente is a ceremonial cloth hand-woven on a horizontal <a href="/wiki/Loom" title="Loom">treadle loom</a> and strips measuring about 4&nbsp;inches wide are sewn together into larger pieces of cloths.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> Cloths come in various colours, sizes and designs and are worn during very important social and religious occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a cultural context, kente is more important than just a cloth and it is a visual representation of history and also a form of written language through weaving.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> The term kente has its roots in the Akan word <i>kɛntɛn</i> which means a basket and the first kente weavers used raffia fibres to weave cloths that looked like kenten (a basket); and thus were referred to as <i>kenten ntoma</i>; meaning basket cloth.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> The original Akan name of the cloth was <i>nsaduaso</i> or <i>nwontoma</i>, meaning "a cloth hand-woven on a loom"; however, "kente" is the most frequently used term today.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth_249-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghanaian_Kente_Cloth-249">[246]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_clothing">Modern clothing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Modern clothing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg/150px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg/225px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg/300px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_men_fashion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2000"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Contemporary Ghanaian men's fashion with Kente and other traditional styles
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg/150px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg/225px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg/300px-Comtemporary_Ghanaian_womenswear.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2000"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Contemporary Ghanaian women's fashion with African print/Ankara and other fabrics
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Contemporary Ghanaian fashion includes traditional and modern styles and fabrics and has made its way into the African and global fashion scene. The cloth known as <a href="/wiki/African_waxprints" class="mw-redirect" title="African waxprints">African print fabric</a> was created out of Dutch wax textiles. It is believed that in the late 1800s, Dutch ships on their way to Asia stocked with machine-made textiles that mimicked Indonesian Batik stopped at many West African ports on the way. The fabrics did not do well in Asia. However, in West Africa – mainly Ghana where there was an already established market for cloths and textiles – the client base grew and it was changed to include local and traditional designs, colours and patterns to cater to the taste of the new consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[247]</a></sup> Today outside of Africa it is called "Ankara" and it has a client base well beyond Ghana and Africa as a whole. It is very popular among Caribbean peoples and African Americans; celebrities such as <a href="/wiki/Solange_Knowles" title="Solange Knowles">Solange Knowles</a> and her sister <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> have been seen wearing African print attire.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[248]</a></sup> Many designers from countries in North America and Europe are now using African prints and it has gained a global interest.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[249]</a></sup> British luxury fashion house <a href="/wiki/Burberry" title="Burberry">Burberry</a> created a collection around Ghanaian styles.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[250]</a></sup> American musician <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> has repeatedly incorporated African prints into her clothing line and can often be seen wearing it.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[251]</a></sup> Internationally acclaimed Ghanaian-British designer <a href="/wiki/Ozwald_Boateng" title="Ozwald Boateng">Ozwald Boateng</a> introduced African print suits in his 2012 collection.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[252]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ghana" title="Music of Ghana">Music of Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azonto" title="Azonto">Azonto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kpanlogo" title="Kpanlogo">Kpanlogo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
