        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Adowa_dance_form_and_music_performance.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Adowa_dance" title="Adowa dance">Adowa dance</a> form and music performance.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ghana" title="Music of Ghana">music of Ghana</a> is diverse and varies between different ethnic groups and regions. Ghanaian music incorporates several distinct types of musical instruments such as the talking drum ensembles, <a href="/wiki/Akan_Drum" title="Akan Drum">Akan Drum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goje" title="Goje">goje</a> fiddle and koloko lute, court music, including the Akan <a href="/wiki/Seperewa" title="Seperewa">Seperewa</a>, the Akan atumpan, the Ga kpanlogo styles, and log <a href="/wiki/Xylophone" title="Xylophone">xylophones</a> used in asonko music.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife-256">[253]</a></sup> The most well known genres to have come from Ghana are African jazz, which was created by Ghanaian artist <a href="/wiki/Guy_Warren" title="Guy Warren">Kofi Ghanaba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[254]</a></sup> and its earliest form of secular music, called <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife-256">[253]</a></sup> Highlife originated in the late 19th century and early 20th century and spread throughout West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife_256-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife-256">[253]</a></sup> In the 1990s a new genre of music was created by the youth incorporating the influences of highlife, Afro-reggae, <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiphop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hiphop">hiphop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife_256-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife-256">[253]</a></sup> This hybrid was called <a href="/wiki/Hiplife" title="Hiplife">hiplife</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife_256-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana:_From_Highlife_to_Hiplife-256">[253]</a></sup> Ghanaian artists such as "Afro Roots" singer, activist and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Dawuni" title="Rocky Dawuni">Rocky Dawuni</a>, R&amp;B and soul singer <a href="/wiki/Rhian_Benson" title="Rhian Benson">Rhian Benson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarkodie_(rapper)" title="Sarkodie (rapper)">Sarkodie</a> have had international success.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhian_Benson's_global_soul_sound_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhian_Benson's_global_soul_sound-258">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sarkodie_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sarkodie-259">[256]</a></sup> In December 2015, Rocky Dawuni became the first Ghanaian musician to be nominated for a Grammy award in the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Reggae_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Reggae Album">Grammy Award for Best Reggae Album</a> category for his 6th studio album titled <i>Branches of The Same Tree</i><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[257]</a></sup> released 31 March 2015. </p>
      <p>Ghanaian dance is as diverse as its music, and there are traditional dances and different dances for different occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Dance,_Ghana_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dance,_Ghana-261">[258]</a></sup> The most known Ghanaian dances are those for celebrations. These dances include the <a href="/wiki/Adowa_dance" title="Adowa dance">Adowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kpanlogo" title="Kpanlogo">Kpanlogo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azonto" title="Azonto">Azonto</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Klama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Klama (page does not exist)">Klama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agbadza" title="Agbadza">Agbadza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borborbor" title="Borborbor">Borborbor</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bamaya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bamaya (page does not exist)">Bamaya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dance,_Ghana_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dance,_Ghana-261">[258]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Nana Otafrija Pallbearing Services, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Dancing_Pallbearers" title="Dancing Pallbearers">Dancing Pallbearers</a>, come from the coastal town of <a href="/wiki/Prampram" title="Prampram">Prampram</a> in the Greater Accra Region of southern Ghana. The group of pallbearers were featured in a BBC feature story in 2017, and footage from the story became part of an Internet meme in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 world pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[259]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:319px;max-width:319px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:101px;max-width:101px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Van_Vicker_(Cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Van_Vicker_%28Cropped%29.jpg/99px-Van_Vicker_%28Cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="99" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Van_Vicker_%28Cropped%29.jpg/149px-Van_Vicker_%28Cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d7/Van_Vicker_%28Cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="179" data-file-height="261"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:110px;max-width:110px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg/108px-Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg" decoding="async" width="108" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg/162px-Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg/216px-Boris_Kodjoe_2010_c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Idris_Elba_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Idris_Elba_2014.jpg/100px-Idris_Elba_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Idris_Elba_2014.jpg/150px-Idris_Elba_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Idris_Elba_2014.jpg/200px-Idris_Elba_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="1944"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <center>
           Popular <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ghanaian_actors" title="List of Ghanaian actors">actor of Ghanaian ancestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Vicker" title="Van Vicker">Van Vicker</a>, and international actors <a href="/wiki/Boris_Kodjoe" title="Boris Kodjoe">Boris Kodjoe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Idris_Elba" title="Idris Elba">Idris Elba</a>
          </center>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana has a budding and thriving film industry. Ghana's film industry dates as far back as 1948 when the Gold Coast Film Unit was set up in the Information Services Department.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[260]</a></sup> Some internationally recognised films have come from Ghana. In 1970, <i>I Told You So</i> was one of the first Ghanaian films to receive international acknowledgement and received great reviews from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[261]</a></sup> It was followed by the 1973 Ghanaian and Italian production <i>The African Deal</i> also known as "<i>Contratto carnale</i>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Bahamian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamian American">Bahamian American</a> actor <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Lockhart" title="Calvin Lockhart">Calvin Lockhart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[262]</a></sup> 1983's <i>Kukurantumi: the Road to Accra</i>, a Ghanaian and German production directed by King Ampaw, was written about by famous American film critic <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Canby" title="Vincent Canby">Vincent Canby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[263]</a></sup> In 1987, <i><a href="/wiki/Cobra_Verde" title="Cobra Verde">Cobra Verde</a></i>, another Ghanaian and German production directed by <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">Werner Herzog</a>, received international acclamation and in 1988, <i>Heritage Africa</i> won more than 12 film awards. </p>
      <p>In recent times there have been collaborations between Ghanaian and Nigerian crew and cast and a number of productions turned out. Many Ghanaian films are co-produced with <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">Nollywood</a>, the Nigerian film industry, and some are distributed by Nigerian marketers. Also, Nigerian filmmakers often feature Ghanaian actors and actresses in their movies and Ghanaian filmmakers feature Nigerian actors and actresses in theirs. <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Buari" title="Nadia Buari">Nadia Buari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Nelson" title="Yvonne Nelson">Yvonne Nelson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lydia_Forson" title="Lydia Forson">Lydia Forson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Appiah" title="Jackie Appiah">Jackie Appiah</a> all popular Ghanaian actresses and <a href="/wiki/Van_Vicker" title="Van Vicker">Van Vicker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Majid_Michel" title="Majid Michel">Majid Michel</a> both popular Ghanaian actors, have starred in many Nigerian movies. As a result of these collaborations, Western viewers often confuse Ghanaian movies with Nollywood and count their sales as one; however, they are two independent industries that sometimes share <i>Nollywood</i>. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Unesco" class="mw-redirect" title="Unesco">UNESCO</a> described Nollywood as the second-biggest film industry in the world after <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[264]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Though The Ghana Film Industry had a downtrend for almost a decade mainly because of low input in production this scenario has drastically change. New and emerging young film makers are adding spice to the already rich Ghana movie scene. Bliz Bazawule,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[265]</a></sup> Peter Sedufia,<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[266]</a></sup> Joseph Clef<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[267]</a></sup> and many others have shown the world the new age of filming in Ghana. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Ghana">Media of Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg/220px-Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg/330px-Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg/440px-Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="310"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghana_Trustworthiness_of_Media.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghana mass media, news and information provided by television.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Ghana">media of Ghana</a> are amongst the most free in Africa. Chapter 12 of the 1992 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ghana" title="Constitution of Ghana">Constitution of Ghana</a> guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a> and independence of the media, while Chapter 2 prohibits censorship.<sup id="cite_ref-gov_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-271">[268]</a></sup> Post-independence, the government and media often had a tense relationship, with private outlets closed during the military governments and strict media laws that prevented criticism of government.<sup id="cite_ref-Anokwa_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anokwa-272">[269]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Press freedoms were restored in 1992, and after the election in 2000 of <a href="/wiki/John_Kufuor" title="John Kufuor">John Agyekum Kufuor</a> the tensions between the private media and government decreased. Kufuor supported press freedom and repealed a <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">libel</a> law, but maintained that the media had to act responsibly.<sup id="cite_ref-pr_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr-273">[270]</a></sup> The Ghanaian media has been described as "one of the most unfettered" in Africa, operating with little restriction. The private press often carries criticism of government policy.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-274">[271]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Ghana" title="Sports in Ghana">Sports in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ghana_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Ghana at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Ghana at the Winter Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_at_the_Olympics" title="Ghana at the Olympics">Ghana at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg/220px-20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg/330px-20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg/440px-20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3599" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20150331_Mali_vs_Ghana_042.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black Stars, the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana national football team</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the top spectator <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Ghana" title="Sports in Ghana">sport in Ghana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">national men's football team</a> is known as the Black Stars, with the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_under-20_football_team" title="Ghana national under-20 football team">under-20 team</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Satellites" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Satellites">Black Satellites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title-275">[272]</a></sup> Ghana has won the <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> four times, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="FIFA U-20 World Cup">FIFA U-20 World Cup</a> once, and has participated in three consecutive <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> in 2006, 2010, and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title-275">[272]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, Ghana became the third African country to reach the quarter-final stage of the World Cup after Cameroon in 1990 and Senegal in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[273]</a></sup> Ghana national U-20 football team, known as the <i>Black Satellites</i>, is considered to be the feeder team for the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana national football team</a>. Ghana is the first and only country on the <a href="/wiki/African_continent" class="mw-redirect" title="African continent">Africa continent</a> to be crowned <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2009 FIFA U-20 World Cup">FIFA U-20 World Cup Champions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title_275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_thrilled_by_historic_title-275">[272]</a></sup> and two-time runners up in <a href="/wiki/1993_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1993 FIFA World Youth Championship">1993</a> and <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="2001 FIFA World Youth Championship">2001</a>. The Ghana national U-17 football team known as the Black Starlets are two-time <a href="/wiki/FIFA_U-17_World_Cup" title="FIFA U-17 World Cup">FIFA U-17 World Cup</a> champions in <a href="/wiki/1991_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="1991 FIFA U-17 World Championship">1991</a> and <a href="/wiki/1995_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="1995 FIFA U-17 World Championship">1995</a>, two-time runners up in <a href="/wiki/1993_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="1993 FIFA U-17 World Championship">1993</a> and <a href="/wiki/1997_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1997 FIFA World Youth Championship">1997</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[274]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_(Ghana_national_football_team).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg/220px-Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg/330px-Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg/440px-Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_%28Ghana_national_football_team%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Stars_Goal_Celebration_(Ghana_national_football_team).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black Stars <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration" title="Goal celebration">goal celebration</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football teams</a> <a href="/wiki/Asante_Kotoko_S.C." title="Asante Kotoko S.C.">Asante Kotoko SC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accra_Hearts_of_Oak_S.C." title="Accra Hearts of Oak S.C.">Accra Hearts of Oak SC</a> are the 5th and 9th best <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football teams</a> on the <a href="/wiki/African_continent" class="mw-redirect" title="African continent">Africa continent</a> and have won a total of five Africa continental association football and <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> trophies; Ghanaian football club <a href="/wiki/Asante_Kotoko_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Asante Kotoko SC">Asante Kotoko SC</a> has been crowned two-time <a href="/wiki/CAF_Champions_League" title="CAF Champions League">CAF Champions League</a> winners in <a href="/wiki/1970_African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" title="1970 African Cup of Champions Clubs">1970</a>, <a href="/wiki/1983_African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" title="1983 African Cup of Champions Clubs">1983</a> and five-time CAF Champions League runners up, and Ghanaian football club <a href="/wiki/Accra_Hearts_of_Oak_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Accra Hearts of Oak SC">Accra Hearts of Oak SC</a> has been crowned <a href="/wiki/2000_CAF_Champions_League" title="2000 CAF Champions League">2000 CAF Champions League</a> winner and two-time CAF Champions League runners up, 2001 <a href="/wiki/CAF_Super_Cup" title="CAF Super Cup">CAF Super Cup</a> champions and <a href="/wiki/2004_CAF_Confederation_Cup" title="2004 CAF Confederation Cup">2004 CAF Confederation Cup</a> champions.<sup id="cite_ref-Africa's_club_of_the_Century_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Africa's_club_of_the_Century-278">[275]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_and_Statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="International Federation of Football History and Statistics">International Federation of Football History and Statistics</a> crowned Asante Kotoko SC as the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_%26_Statistics#Continental_Clubs_of_the_20th_century" title="International Federation of Football History &amp; Statistics">African club of the 20th century</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Africa's_club_of_the_Century_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Africa's_club_of_the_Century-278">[275]</a></sup> There are several club football teams in Ghana that play in the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Premier_League" title="Ghana Premier League">Ghana Premier League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Football_Leagues" title="Ghana Football Leagues">Division One League</a>, both administered by the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Football_Association" title="Ghana Football Association">Ghana Football Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[276]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg/220px-2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg/330px-2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg/440px-2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1207" data-file-height="1206"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2010_Opening_Ceremony_-_Ghana_entering.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter sport">winter sports</a> Olympic team at the <a href="/wiki/Opening_ceremony" title="Opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ghana competed in the Winter Olympics in 2010 for the first time. Ghana qualified for the 2010 Winter Olympics, scoring 137.5 <a href="/wiki/International_Ski_Federation" title="International Ski Federation">International Ski Federation</a> points, within the qualifying range of 120–140 points.<sup id="cite_ref-0-21_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-0-21-280">[277]</a></sup> Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah-Acheampong" title="Kwame Nkrumah-Acheampong">Kwame Nkrumah-Acheampong</a>, nicknamed "The <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopard</a>", became the first <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian</a> to take part in the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, British Columbia, Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-281">[278]</a></sup> taking part in the <a href="/wiki/Slalom_skiing" title="Slalom skiing">slalom skiing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vancouver_2010_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vancouver_2010-282">[279]</a></sup> Ghana finished 47th out of 102 participating nations, of whom 54 finished in the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_slalom" title="Alpine skiing at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Men's slalom">Alpine skiing slalom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Results_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Results-284">[281]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah-Acheampong" title="Kwame Nkrumah-Acheampong">Kwame Nkrumah-Acheampong</a> broke on the international <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> circuit, being the second <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black African</a> skier to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana's_first_winter_Olympian_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana's_first_winter_Olympian-285">[282]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's last medal at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> dates back to 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[283]</a></sup> Ghanaian athletes have won a total of four Olympics medals in thirteen appearances at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a>, three in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Bronze_medal" title="Bronze medal">bronze medal</a> in association football, and thus became the first country on the <a href="/wiki/African_continent" class="mw-redirect" title="African continent">Africa continent</a> to win a medal at association football.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_Olympic_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_Olympic-287">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana competes in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>, sending athletes in every edition since <a href="/wiki/1954_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1954 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1954</a> (except for the <a href="/wiki/1986_Commonwealth_Games" title="1986 Commonwealth Games">1986 games</a>). Ghana has won fifty-seven medals at the Commonwealth Games, including fifteen gold, with all but one of their medals coming in athletics and boxing. </p>
      <p>The country has also produced a number of world class boxers, including <a href="/wiki/Azumah_Nelson" title="Azumah Nelson">Azumah Nelson</a> a three-time world champion and considered as Africa's greatest <a href="/wiki/Boxer" class="mw-redirect" title="Boxer">boxer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[285]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers-289">[286]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nana_Konadu" title="Nana Konadu">Nana Yaw Konadu</a> also a three-time world champion,<sup id="cite_ref-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers-289">[286]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ike_Quartey" title="Ike Quartey">Ike Quartey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers_289-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers-289">[286]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Clottey" title="Joshua Clottey">Joshua Clottey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers_289-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_5_Ghanaian_Boxers-289">[286]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana's women's football team won bronze at the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Women_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Women Cup of Nations">Africa Women Cup of Nations</a> 2016 edition in Yaoundé, Cameroon. The team beat South Africa 1–0.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[287]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> Ghana will host the <a href="/wiki/2023_African_Games" title="2023 African Games">2023 African Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>.</p>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage_and_architecture">Cultural heritage and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Cultural heritage and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ghana%27s_material_cultural_heritage" title="Ghana's material cultural heritage">Ghana's material cultural heritage</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Ghana" title="List of museums in Ghana">Ghanaian museums</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_(Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG/220px-Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG/330px-Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG/440px-Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_%28Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="449"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghan%C3%A9s_Arquitectura_Postmoderna_y_Arquitectura_Futurista_(Ghanaian_Postmodern_Architecture_and_Futurist_Architecture).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">postmodern architecture</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Accra_Skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Accra, 2019" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Accra_Skyline.jpg/220px-Accra_Skyline.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Accra_Skyline.jpg/330px-Accra_Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Accra_Skyline.jpg/440px-Accra_Skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Accra_Skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Accra, 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are two types of Ghanaian traditional construction: the series of adjacent buildings in an enclosure around a common are common and the traditional round huts with grass roof.<sup id="cite_ref-ARC_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARC-291">[288]</a></sup> The round huts with grass roof architecture are situated in the northern regions of Ghana (<a href="/wiki/Northern_Region_(Ghana)" title="Northern Region (Ghana)">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Region" title="Upper East Region">Upper East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_West_Region" title="Upper West Region">Upper West</a> regions), while the series of adjacent buildings are in the southern regions of Ghana (<a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Region" title="Ashanti Region">Ashanti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brong-Ahafo_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brong-Ahafo Region">Brong-Ahafo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Region_(Ghana)" title="Central Region (Ghana)">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Region_(Ghana)" title="Eastern Region (Ghana)">Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Accra_Region" title="Greater Accra Region">Greater Accra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Region_(Ghana)" title="Western Region (Ghana)">Western</a> regions).<sup id="cite_ref-ARC_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARC-291">[288]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">postmodern architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/High-tech_architecture" title="High-tech architecture">high-tech architecture</a> buildings are predominant in the Ghanaian southern regions, while the Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="Heritage site">heritage sites</a> are most evident by the more than thirty <a href="/wiki/Fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort">forts</a> and castles built in Ghana. Some of these forts are <a href="/wiki/Fort_William_(fort)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort William (fort)">Fort William</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam_(Ghana)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Amsterdam (Ghana)">Fort Amsterdam</a>. Ghana has museums that are situated inside castles, and two are situated inside a fort.<sup id="cite_ref-Museums_and_Monuments_Board_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museums_and_Monuments_Board-292">[289]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_Museum_(Ghana)" title="Armed Forces Museum (Ghana)">Military Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Ghana" title="National Museum of Ghana">National Museum</a> organise temporary exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-Museums_and_Monuments_Board_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museums_and_Monuments_Board-292">[289]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ghana has museums that show a in-depth look at specific <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Ghana" title="Regions of Ghana">Ghanaian regions</a>, there are a number of museums that provide insight into the traditions and history of their own geographical area in Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-Museums_and_Monuments_Board_292-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museums_and_Monuments_Board-292">[289]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coast_Castle" title="Cape Coast Castle">Cape Coast Castle</a> Museum and St. Georges Castle (<a href="/wiki/Elmina_Castle" title="Elmina Castle">Elmina Castle</a>) Museum offer <a href="/wiki/Guided_tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Guided tour">guided tours</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Kwame Nkrumah University of Science and Technology">Museum of Science and Technology</a> provides its visitors with a look into the domain of Ghanaian <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific</a> development, through exhibits of objects of scientific and <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technological</a> interest.<sup id="cite_ref-Museums_and_Monuments_Board_292-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museums_and_Monuments_Board-292">[289]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">National symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: National symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tawny_Eagle_(Aquila_rapax)_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg/220px-Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg/330px-Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg/440px-Tawny_Eagle_%28Aquila_rapax%29_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="531"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tawny_Eagle_(Aquila_rapax)_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <center>
          The <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagle</a> appears on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Ghana" title="Coat of arms of Ghana">coat of arms of Ghana</a>.
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Ghana" title="Coat of arms of Ghana">coat of arms</a> depicts two animals: the <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagle</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Aquila_rapax" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquila rapax">Aquila rapax</a></i>, a very large <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey">bird</a> that lives in the savannas and deserts;<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[290]</a></sup> 35% of Ghana's <a href="/wiki/Land_mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Land mass">landmass</a> is <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>, 35% is forest, 30% is <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a>) and the lion (<i><a href="/wiki/Panthera_leo" class="mw-redirect" title="Panthera leo">Panthera leo</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Big_cat" title="Big cat">big cat</a>); a <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_sword" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceremonial sword">ceremonial sword</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Heraldic" class="mw-redirect" title="Heraldic">heraldic</a> castle on a heraldic sea, a <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Cocoa tree">cocoa tree</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Mine_shaft" class="mw-redirect" title="Mine shaft">mine shaft</a> representing the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial mineral</a> wealth of Ghana, and a five-pointed black star rimmed with gold representing the mineral gold wealth of Ghana and the lodestar of the <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_people" title="Ghanaian people">Ghanaian people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_National_Emblems_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_National_Emblems-294">[291]</a></sup> It also has the legend <i>Freedom and Justice</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_National_Emblems_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_National_Emblems-294">[291]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Ghana" title="Flag of Ghana">flag of Ghana</a> consists of three horizontal bands (strips) of red (top), gold (middle) and green (bottom); the three bands are the same height and width; the middle band bears a five-pointed black <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">star</a> in the centre of the gold band, the colour red band stands for the blood spilled to achieve the nation's independence: gold stands for Ghana's <a href="/wiki/Industrial_mineral" title="Industrial mineral">industrial mineral</a> wealth, and the colour green symbolises the rich <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforests</a> and natural resources of Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_flag_and_description_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_flag_and_description-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_National_Emblems_294-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_National_Emblems-294">[291]</a></sup></p>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Ghana" title="Tourism in Ghana">Tourism in Ghana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region,_Ghana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg/220px-Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg/330px-Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg/440px-Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region%2C_Ghana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Surfers_Surfing_at_Busua_Beach_in_Western_region,_Ghana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Surfer" class="mw-redirect" title="Surfer">Surfers</a> <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_wave_surfing" title="Big wave surfing">big wave surfing</a> at <a href="/wiki/Busua_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Busua Beach">Busua Beach</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Region_(Ghana)" title="Western Region (Ghana)">Western region</a><sup id="cite_ref-11_of_the_world's_most_unusual_surf_spots_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11_of_the_world's_most_unusual_surf_spots-295">[292]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2011, 1,087,000 tourists visited Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-WAO_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WAO-296">[293]</a></sup> Tourist arrivals to Ghana include South Americans, Asians, Europeans, and North Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-Trade_Expo_International_Ghana_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trade_Expo_International_Ghana-297">[294]</a></sup> The attractions and major tourist destinations of Ghana include a warm, tropical climate year-round, diverse wildlife, waterfalls such as <a href="/wiki/Kintampo_waterfalls" title="Kintampo waterfalls">Kintampo waterfalls</a> and the largest waterfall in west Africa, <a href="/wiki/Wli_waterfalls" title="Wli waterfalls">Wli waterfalls</a>, Ghana's coastal palm-lined sandy beaches, caves, mountains, rivers, and reservoirs and lakes such as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Bosumtwi" title="Lake Bosumtwi">Lake Bosumtwi</a> and the largest man-made lake in the world by surface area, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Volta" title="Lake Volta">Lake Volta</a>, dozens of <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Ghana" title="List of castles in Ghana">forts and castles</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>, nature reserves and national parks.<sup id="cite_ref-Trade_Expo_International_Ghana_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trade_Expo_International_Ghana-297">[294]</a></sup> Aside the beautiful natural reserves which serves as a tourist site, there are some <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castles</a> in Ghana that also serve as tourist sites which attracts many <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourists</a> from all over the world. Some of the notable castles are <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coast_Castle_Museum" title="Cape Coast Castle Museum">Cape Coast Castle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Elmina_Castle" title="Elmina Castle">Elmina Castle</a> all in the Central region of Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[295]</a></sup> Not only are the castles important for tourism but also serve as mark for remembering our <a href="/wiki/Ancestor" title="Ancestor">forefathers</a> whose blood were shed and sacrifices made to preserve and promote the black or African heritage which was robbed through the slave trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Centre_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centre-299">[296]</a></sup> As a result of this, the World Heritage Convention of UNESCO named Ghana's castles and forts as World Heritage Monuments.<sup id="cite_ref-Centre_299-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centre-299">[296]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> statistics in 2010 showed that out of the world's favorite tourist destinations, Ghana was ranked 108th out of 139 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-RANK_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RANK-300">[297]</a></sup> The country had moved two places up from the 2009 rankings. In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine, published that Ghana was ranked the eleventh most friendly country in the world. The assertion was based on a survey in 2010 of a cross-section of travellers. Of all the African countries that were included in the survey, Ghana ranked highest.<sup id="cite_ref-RANK_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RANK-300">[297]</a></sup> Tourism is the fourth highest earner of foreign exchange for the country.<sup id="cite_ref-RANK_300-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RANK-300">[297]</a></sup> In 2017, Ghana ranks as the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">43rd–most peaceful country</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Global_Peace_Index_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Global_Peace_Index-301">[298]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>To enter Ghana, it is necessary to have a visa authorized by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ghana" title="Government of Ghana">Government of Ghana</a>. Travellers must apply for this visa at a Ghanaian embassy; this process can take approximately two weeks. By law, visitors entering Ghana must be able to produce a yellow fever vaccination certificate.<sup id="cite_ref-travel_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travel-302">[299]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Destination Pride<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[300]</a></sup> – a data-driven search platform used to visualize the world's LGBTQ+ laws, rights and social sentiment – Ghana's Pride score is 22 (out of 100).<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[301]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:608px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama view of Kakum National Park, located in the coastal environs of the Central region on the Gulf of Guinea and Atlantic Ocean, covers an area of 375 square kilometres (145&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Established in 1931 as a game reserve and nature reserve, it was gazetted as a national park only in 1992 after an initial survey of avifauna was conducted. The national park is covered with tropical rainforest. Kakum National Park is the only national park in Africa with a canopy walkway, which is 350 metres (1,150&nbsp;ft) long and connects seven canopy tree tops which provides access to the rainforests."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg/600px-Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg" decoding="async" width="600" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg/900px-Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg/1200px-Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3621" data-file-height="1080"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_view_of_Kakum_Nationalpark.jpg" title="File:Panorama view of Kakum Nationalpark.jpg"> </a>
         </div>Panorama view of <a href="/wiki/Kakum_National_Park" title="Kakum National Park">Kakum National Park</a>, located in the coastal environs of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Region_(Ghana)" title="Central Region (Ghana)">Central region</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and Atlantic Ocean, covers an area of 375 square kilometres (145&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Established in 1931 as a <a href="/wiki/Game_reserve" title="Game reserve">game reserve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a>, it was <a href="/wiki/Gazetted" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazetted">gazetted</a> as a national park only in 1992 after an initial survey of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">avifauna</a> was conducted. The national park is covered with tropical rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-Parks_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parks-305">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unesco_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unesco-306">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NGO_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NGO-307">[304]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kakum_National_Park" title="Kakum National Park">Kakum National Park</a> is the only national park in Africa with a <a href="/wiki/Canopy_walkway" title="Canopy walkway">canopy walkway</a>, which is 350 metres (1,150&nbsp;ft) long and connects seven <a href="/wiki/Canopy_(biology)" title="Canopy (biology)">canopy</a> tree <a href="/wiki/Crown_(botany)" title="Crown (botany)">tops</a> which provides access to the <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Unesco_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unesco-306">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Life_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life-308">[305]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

            <tr> 
             <td style="background:#71b37b;width:5px"> </td> 
             <td><a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ghana#Low_Plains" title="Geography of Ghana">Coastal Plain</a> </td> 
             <td><a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apam" title="Apam">Apam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coast" title="Cape Coast">Cape Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">Elmina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kakum_National_Park" title="Kakum National Park">Kakum National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kokrobite" title="Kokrobite">Kokrobite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nzulezo" title="Nzulezo">Nzulezo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sekondi-Takoradi" title="Sekondi-Takoradi">Sekondi-Takoradi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ada_Foah" title="Ada Foah">Ada Foah</a> </td> 
             <td>The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> <a href="/wiki/Coastal_plain" title="Coastal plain">coastal plain</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_government" title="Seat of government">seat of government</a> and capital city, several castles and forts and the best preserved <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> in Ghana </td>

             <td><a href="/wiki/Koforidua" title="Koforidua">Koforidua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumasi" title="Kumasi">Kumasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obuasi" title="Obuasi">Obuasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunyani" title="Sunyani">Sunyani</a> </td>

             <td>massive and world's largest <a href="/wiki/Lake_Volta" title="Lake Volta">Lake Volta</a>, the river system that feeds it and Ghana eastern <a href="/wiki/Border_crossing" class="mw-redirect" title="Border crossing">border crossing</a> </td>

             <td><a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">Savanna</a> plains and north Ghana <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade route</a> and <a href="/wiki/Border_crossing" class="mw-redirect" title="Border crossing">border crossing</a> </td>

        </tr>

        </tr>
